Ibadiyya on Free Will, Creation of Acts, and Eschatology
Ibadiyya on capacity before act, creation of acts, world's end, and children.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ibadiyya doctrines on human capacity before the act, creation of acts by Allah, and the end of the world.

Core Idea
The Ibadiyya affirmed that capacity precedes the act and that acts are created by Allah, and the world ends with the obligation.

This lesson covers three additional Ibadiyya positions: that human capacity (istiṭāʿa) exists before the act, that human acts are created by God, and that the entire world perishes when the original obligation ends. These views align with certain theological schools. The lesson also addresses their suspension of judgment on disbelievers' children.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on capacity, creation, and eschatology
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the three distinct doctrines: istiṭāʿa before act, act created by Allah, world perishes.
Also note the final point about children of disbelievers.
2
Understand the doctrine of capacity (istiṭāʿa)
The phrase 'الاستطاعة قبل الفعل' means human capacity precedes the act, implying the act is performed with that capacity.
This is similar to the Ash'ari position.
3
Understand the creation of human acts
'فعل العبد مخلوق لله' means that human actions are created by Allah. This affirms divine omnipotence.
4
Understand the eschatological doctrine
'يفنى العالم كله بفناء أصل التكليف' suggests the world ends when the original obligation ends—a unique view.
5
Note the suspension on children
They refrained from declaring children of disbelievers and torturing them, showing a cautious attitude.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأباضية هو عبد الله بن أباض قالوا مخالفونا من أهل القبلة كفار غير مشركين يجوز مناكحتهم وغنيمة أموالهم من سلاحهم وكراعهم حلال عند الحرب دون غيره ودارهم دار الإسلام إلا معسكر سلطانهم وقالوا تقبل شهادة مخالفيهم عليهم ومرتكب الكبيرة موحد غير مؤمن بناء على أن الأعمال داخلة في الإيمان والاستطاعة قبل الفعل وفعل العبد مخلوق لله تعالى ويفنى العالم كله بفناء أصل التكليف ومرتكب الكبيرة كافر كفر نعمة لا ملة وتوقفوا في تكفير أولاد الكفار وتعذيبهم.
The Ibāḍiyya – its founder was ʿAbdallāh ibn Ibāḍ. They said: Our opponents among the people of the qibla are disbelievers but not polytheists; it is permissible to marry them, and the spoils of their property – from their weapons and horses – are lawful during war but not otherwise. Their abode is the abode of Islam except for the camp of their ruler. And they said: The testimony of opponents is accepted against them. The committer of grave sins is a monotheist but not a believer, based on the principle that works are included in faith. And capacity (al-istiṭāʿa) is before the act. The servant's act is created by God. The entire world perishes with the perishing of the original obligation. The committer of grave sins is a disbeliever of ingratitude (kufr niʿma), not of religion (milla). And they refrained from declaring the children of disbelievers disbelievers and torturing them.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage describes the doctrines of the Ibāḍiyya, founded by ʿAbdallāh ibn Ibāḍ. They considered other Muslims (ahl al-qibla) who disagree with them to be disbelievers, but not polytheists, allowing intermarriage and taking of spoils in war. Their territory is considered Islamic except for the ruler's camp. They accept testimony of opponents against their own members. The Ibāḍiyya held that works are part of faith, so a grave sinner is a muwaḥḥid (monotheist) but not a muʾmin (believer). They affirmed that human capacity (istiṭāʿa) precedes the act, that human acts are created by God, and that the entire world perishes when the original obligation ends. Grave sinners are guilty of kufr niʿma (disbelief of ingratitude) rather than kufr milla (disbelief of religion). Finally, they suspend judgment on the status of unbelievers' children and their punishment.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة
قبل الفعل
فعل العبد
مخلوق
فناء العالم
أصل التكليف
أولاد الكفار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ibadiyya deny human free will because they say acts are created by Allah.
Correction: They affirm human capacity prior to the act, which preserves human responsibility.

Checkpoint
What does the Ibadiyya mean by 'الاستطاعة قبل الفعل'?
A) Capacity after the act
B) Capacity before the act
C) No capacity
D) Capacity both before and after

Key Takeaway
The Ibadiyya held that human capacity precedes the act, acts are created by Allah, the world ends with the obligation, and they suspend judgment on disbelievers' children.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that every act of yours is created by Allah, how would that change the way you react to your own failures or sins? Would you still feel the weight of personal responsibility, or would you use divine decree as an excuse? What specific step will you take today to embrace both divine omnipotence and your own accountability?
?
The Ibadiyya suspend judgment on the children of disbelievers, refusing to declare their fate. Is there someone in your life—perhaps a non-Muslim relative or a person with different beliefs—whom you have already judged in your heart? How can you follow the Ibadiyya's cautious example and leave their ultimate fate to Allah alone?
?
The world, according to the Ibadiyya, has a purpose tied to divine commands. Reflect for a moment: are you living as if your life on earth has a specific purpose from Allah? If you were told that your personal 'world' would end the moment you abandon His commands, what would you change right now?

Khawarij Legal Extremes: Killing, Stoning, and Qadhf
Enumeration of three legal doctrines of the Khawarij: killing opponents, no stoning, and qadhf rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Khawarij positions on killing opponents' children and women, rejection of stoning for adultery, and their modified ruling on false accusation (qadhf).

Core Idea
Khawarij redefined Islamic legal punishments based on literalist and selective interpretation of the Quran.

This conclusion of the fourth observatory lists several extreme Khawarij doctrines that depart from mainstream Sunni consensus. The first set concerns physical punishments—killing, stoning, and flogging for false accusation. As you read, notice how they justify their rejection of stoning and their gendered approach to qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage from 'خاتمة' to 'وهذا أظهر'. Pay attention to the key terms: قتل أولاد المخالفين, رجم, حد القذف.
2
Identify three legal rulings
Identify the three rulings mentioned: killing opponents' families, rejection of stoning, and the modification of qadhf.
Notice that each ruling is distinct.
3
Analyze the qadhf reasoning
Understand why they exempt women from qadhf: the Quran uses masculine plural 'alladhina'. Also note Al-Amidi's addition about dropping hadd for accusers of chaste men.
4
Consider the implications
Reflect on how these rulings contrast with mainstream Islamic law. The commentary will highlight the departures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة للمرصد الرابع قتل أولاد المخالفين ونسائهم، ولا رجم على الزاني المحصن إذ هو غير مذكور في القرآن ) ولا حد للقذف على النساء ) أي القاذف إن كان امرأة لم يحد لأن المذكور في القرآن هو صيغة الذين وهو للمذكرين قال الآمدي وأسقطوا حد قذف المحصنين من الرجال دون النساء أي المقذوف المحصن إن كان رجلاً لا يحد قاذفه وإن كان امرأة يحد قاذفها وهذا أظهر ) وأطفال المشركين في النار مع آبائهم ويجوز نبي كان كافراً وإن علم كفره بعد النبوة، ومرتكب الكبيرة كافر.
Conclusion of the fourth observatory: Killing the children of opponents and their women, and no stoning for the married adulterer since it is not mentioned in the Quran, and no hadd for false accusation (qadhf) against women: i.e., if the accuser is a woman she is not flogged because what is mentioned in the Quran is the masculine plural form 'alladhina' which refers to males. Al-Amidi said: 'And they dropped the hadd of qadhf for chaste men but not for women, i.e., if the chaste person who is accused is a man, his accuser is not flogged, but if it is a woman, her accuser is flogged, and this is more apparent.' And the children of polytheists are in the Fire with their fathers, and it is permissible that a prophet was a disbeliever even if his disbelief is known after prophethood, and the committer of a major sin is a disbeliever.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion listing some Khawarij doctrines. It states that they kill the children and women of opponents, reject stoning for adultery because it is not in the Quran, and eliminate hadd for qadhf against women. The commentator explains the reasoning: the Quranic verse uses masculine plural, so women are excluded. Al-Amidi is quoted saying they dropped hadd for chaste men but not for women. Then it mentions that children of polytheists are in Hell with their fathers, and that it is possible for a prophet to have been a disbeliever after prophethood (a deviant view). Finally, the committer of a major sin is considered a disbeliever. This passage summarizes extreme Khawarij positions.

Key Terms
رجم
حد القذف
قتل أولاد المخالفين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all Khawarij held these exact legal views uniformly.
Correction: This passage describes the views of certain early Khawarij groups; later Khawarij sects differed on many rulings.

Checkpoint
What is the Khawarij ruling on stoning for a married adulterer according to this passage?
A) They affirm stoning as the punishment.
B) They reject stoning because it is not mentioned in the Quran.
C) They increase the punishment to death by sword.
D) They replace stoning with flogging.

Key Takeaway
The Khawarij selectively applied Quranic texts to reject stoning and limit the qadhf punishment based on gender and victim status.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. The Khawarij used a literal reading of the Quran to justify abandoning a punishment (stoning) while justifying killing innocent families. Where in your own life do you twist scripture or tradition to suit your desires? Will you commit this week to honestly examining one area where you might be doing the same?
?
2. Their selective literalism exempted women from punishment for false accusations, claiming 'alladhina' only refers to men. Are there verses or teachings you ignore because they don't match your assumptions about gender or justice? How will you confront that discomfort today?
?
3. The Khawarij's errors led to extreme injustice—both harshness and leniency. Think of a time you were either too harsh or too lenient in applying Islamic teachings to yourself or others. What specific step can you take this week to seek the balanced middle path (wasatiyya) that the Quran commands?

Khawarij Theological Extremes: Children, Prophets, and Major Sinners
Enumeration of three theological doctrines: children in Hell, prophet's potential disbelief, takfir of major sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Khawarij positions on the fate of polytheist children, the possibility of a prophet's disbelief after prophethood, and the takfir of major sinners.

Core Idea
Khawarij held extreme theological views on salvation and faith, including that children of polytheists are in Hell and that major sins cause disbelief.

This concluding passage of the fourth observatory also lists several theological doctrines of the Khawarij regarding the afterlife of children, the impeccability of prophets, and the definition of faith. These positions starkly contrast with mainstream Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage from ') وأطفال المشركين' to the end. Notice the three distinct doctrines.
2
Identify the three theological claims
Identify the claims about children of polytheists, prophets, and major sinners. Each is a separate extreme position.
3
Reflect on the prophet doctrine
Consider the grave implication of saying a prophet could become a disbeliever after prophethood. This contradicts the universal Islamic belief in prophetic impeccability.
4
Connect to Khawarij core principle
Understand that the takfir of major sinners is the foundational belief of Khawarij, linking sin with disbelief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة للمرصد الرابع قتل أولاد المخالفين ونسائهم، ولا رجم على الزاني المحصن إذ هو غير مذكور في القرآن ) ولا حد للقذف على النساء ) أي القاذف إن كان امرأة لم يحد لأن المذكور في القرآن هو صيغة الذين وهو للمذكرين قال الآمدي وأسقطوا حد قذف المحصنين من الرجال دون النساء أي المقذوف المحصن إن كان رجلاً لا يحد قاذفه وإن كان امرأة يحد قاذفها وهذا أظهر ) وأطفال المشركين في النار مع آبائهم ويجوز نبي كان كافراً وإن علم كفره بعد النبوة، ومرتكب الكبيرة كافر.
Conclusion of the fourth observatory: Killing the children of opponents and their women, and no stoning for the married adulterer since it is not mentioned in the Quran, and no hadd for false accusation (qadhf) against women: i.e., if the accuser is a woman she is not flogged because what is mentioned in the Quran is the masculine plural form 'alladhina' which refers to males. Al-Amidi said: 'And they dropped the hadd of qadhf for chaste men but not for women, i.e., if the chaste person who is accused is a man, his accuser is not flogged, but if it is a woman, her accuser is flogged, and this is more apparent.' And the children of polytheists are in the Fire with their fathers, and it is permissible that a prophet was a disbeliever even if his disbelief is known after prophethood, and the committer of a major sin is a disbeliever.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion listing some Khawarij doctrines. It states that they kill the children and women of opponents, reject stoning for adultery because it is not in the Quran, and eliminate hadd for qadhf against women. The commentator explains the reasoning: the Quranic verse uses masculine plural, so women are excluded. Al-Amidi is quoted saying they dropped hadd for chaste men but not for women. Then it mentions that children of polytheists are in Hell with their fathers, and that it is possible for a prophet to have been a disbeliever after prophethood (a deviant view). Finally, the committer of a major sin is considered a disbeliever. This passage summarizes extreme Khawarij positions.

Key Terms
أطفال المشركين
مرتكب الكبيرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Khawarij only differed on political issues, not theology.
Correction: This passage shows they held extreme theological views on children, prophets, and sin, which are foundational to their identity.

Checkpoint
According to the Khawarij as stated in this passage, what happens to the children of polytheists?
A) They are not judged and enter Paradise.
B) They remain in a state of limbo.
C) They are in the Fire with their fathers.
D) They are reincarnated as believers.

Key Takeaway
The Khawarij believed that children of polytheists go to Hell, that prophets can fall into disbelief, and that major sins expel one from faith entirely.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Khawarij taught that committing a major sin makes you a disbeliever. Is there a sin in your life that you have allowed to make you feel utterly cut off from Allah? How does the mainstream teaching on repentance (tawba) and Allah's vast mercy challenge that feeling? Will you sincerely turn back to Him today, or will you let the Khawarij's harsh judgment linger in your heart?
?
The Khawarij judged children of polytheists to be in Hell. Are there people—perhaps those from non-Muslim backgrounds or those who have wronged you—whom you have mentally condemned as beyond hope? How does this lesson expose the danger of making such absolute judgments? Will you actively work to see others through the lens of Allah's mercy rather than your own verdict?
?
The Khawarij thought a prophet could fall into disbelief. Consider your own attitude toward religious authority or scholars you respect. Do you ever scrutinize their minor mistakes as if they invalidate their entire guidance? How does the Khawarij's extreme view on prophets mirror your own tendency to dismiss others over small errors? Will you commit to distinguishing between human fallibility and disbelief, and extend the same grace you hope for from Allah?

Najdiyya and 'Adhiriyya: Excusing Ignorance in Subsidiary Matters
Historical account and doctrinal summary of Najdiyya and 'Adhiriyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the 'Adhiriyya doctrine of excusing ignorance in subsidiary religious matters and the Najdiyya view on imamate.

Core Idea
Ignorance is excused in subsidiary matters but not in essentials.

This lesson explores a specific sectarian position within the Kharijites: the Najdiyya, and their subgroup the 'Adhiriyya. Originating from an incident where Najda ibn 'Amir excused his soldiers' ignorance of proper conduct in war, they developed a clear distinction between essential and subsidiary religious knowledge. Understanding this distinction helps clarify how early theological debates defined the limits of excusable ignorance.

Guided Path
1
Read the story of Najda's army
Begin by reading the account of what happened with the army in al-Qatif. This historical incident is the context for the doctrine.
2
Identify the two categories of religion
Notice how the 'Adhiriyya divided religious matters into two categories: essential knowledge and subsidiary matters. Determine which category allows for excusing ignorance.
Essential knowledge includes knowledge of God, His Messenger, and prohibition of Muslim blood.
3
Examine their view on leadership
The Najdiyya held that an imam is not obligatory; fairness among people suffices. Consider how this contrasts with other groups.
They only allow appointing an imam if necessary for maintaining fairness.
4
Compare with the Azariqa
The passage notes that the Najdiyya agreed with the Azariqa on takfir but differed on other rulings. Reflect on the significance of this partial agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النجدية: هو نجدة بن عامر النجفي، منهم العاذرية: الذين عذروا الناس بالجهالات في الفروع. وذلك أن نجدة وجه ابنه مع جيش إلى أهل القطيف فقتلوهم وأسروا نساءهم ونكحوهن قبل القسمة وأكلوا من الغنيمة قبلها أيضا، فلما رجعوا إلى نجدة أخبروه بما فعلوا فقال: لم يسعكم ما فعلتم فقالوا: لم نعلم أن لا يسعنا فعذرهم بجهالتهم فاختلف أصحابه بعد ذلك فمنهم من تابعه وقالوا الدين أمران: أحدهما معرفة الله ورسوله وتحريم دماء المسلمين أي الموافقين لهم والإقرار بما جاء به الرسول جملة فهذا لا يعذر فيه الجاهل به والثاني: ما سوى ذلك الجاهل به معذور. فهؤلاء منهم سموا عاذرية. وقالوا: أي النجدات كلهم لا حاجة للناس إلى الإمام بل الواجب عليهم رعاية النصفة فيما بينهم ويجوز لهم نصبه إذا رأوا أن تلك الرعاية تتم إلا بإمام يحملهم عليها. وخالفوا الأزارقة في غير التكفير أي وافقوهم في التكفير وخالفوهم في الأحكام الباقية.
Najdiyya: He is Najda ibn 'Amir al-Najafi. Among them are the 'Adhiriyya: those who excuse people for ignorances in subsidiary matters. That is because Najda sent his son with an army to the people of al-Qatif, and they killed them, took their women captive, had intercourse with them before division, and ate from the spoils before division. When they returned to Najda, they informed him of what they did. He said, 'What you did is not permissible.' They said, 'We did not know that it was not permissible.' So he excused them due to their ignorance. Then his companions differed after that. Some of them followed him and said: Religion consists of two matters: one is knowledge of God and His Messenger, and the prohibition of the blood of Muslims, i.e., those who agree with them, and affirmation of what the Messenger brought in general; this is not excused for the ignorant. The second is everything else; the ignorant is excused. So these among them are called 'Adhiriyya. And they said, i.e., all Najdites: There is no need for people for an Imam; rather it is obligatory upon them to maintain fairness among themselves, and it is permissible for them to appoint [an Imam] if they see that this fairness is only accomplished through an Imam who compels them to it. And they differed from the Azariqa in matters other than takfir, i.e., they agreed with them in takfir but differed in the remaining rulings.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage describes the Najdiyya sect, founded by Najda ibn 'Amir. The 'Adhiriyya subgroup originated from an incident where Najda's army acted ignorantly, and he excused them. They then formulated a doctrine: religious matters are divided into two categories: essential (knowledge of God, His Messenger, prohibition of Muslim blood) where ignorance is not excused, and subsidiary (furu') where ignorance is excused. This made them 'excusers' ('Adhiriyya). The Najdiyya as a whole held that an Imam is not obligatory; they only appoint one if needed for fairness. They agreed with the Azariqa in takfir but disagreed on other points.

Key Terms
النجدية
العاذرية
الجهالات في الفروع
الدين أمران
الإمام
النصفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the 'Adhiriyya excuse ignorance in all religious matters.
Correction: They only excuse ignorance in subsidiary matters (furu'), not in essential knowledge of God, His Messenger, and prohibition of Muslim blood.

Checkpoint
According to the 'Adhiriyya, in which category of religious matters is ignorance not excused?
A) All matters
B) Subsidiary matters (furu')
C) Knowledge of God and His Messenger and prohibition of Muslim blood
D) None

Key Takeaway
The 'Adhiriyya divided religious matters into essential and subsidiary, excusing ignorance only in the latter, and the Najdiyya held that an imam is not obligatory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which matters of your faith do you consider essential? Have you settled your knowledge of God and His Messenger, or do you assume you know them well enough? This passage from the 'Adhiriyya teaches that ignorance in essentials is not excused. Will you examine yourself today and identify one essential truth you have neglected, and commit to learning it?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim making a mistake in a subsidiary religious practice, do you rush to condemn or do you make excuses based on their ignorance, as the 'Adhiriyya did? This lesson challenges you to reflect on your own reaction. Remember, you yourself are ignorant in many matters. Will you adopt a more compassionate approach starting today?
?
The Najdiyya argued that people have no inherent need for an imam, yet they admitted it might be necessary for fairness. In your own life, do you recognize the need for legitimate religious leadership and guidance, or do you operate as if you are self-sufficient? This passage forces you to consider your attitude towards authority. What is one step you will take to connect with legitimate religious guidance?

Sufriyya: Views on Takfir, Rajm, and Taqiyya
Description of Sufriyya doctrines and differences from Azariqa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinctive doctrines of the Sufriyya sect, particularly their positions on takfir, stoning, children of disbelievers, taqiyya, and the classification of sins.

Core Idea
The Sufriyya nuanced takfir and sin classification, allowing for specific labels without outright excommunication.

The Sufriyya were a Kharijite sub-sect who differed from the Azariqa on several key issues. This passage from al-Mawaqif outlines their distinctive views on takfir, stoning, children of disbelievers, taqiyya, and how sins are classified. Understanding these nuances helps clarify intra-sectarian debates within early Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sect and its founder
The Sufriyya are followers of Ziyad ibn al-Asfar. Learn their name and origin.
They are a Kharijite sub-sect.
2
Compare with Azariqa on three points
Note the differences: they do not declare takfir of those who sit out fighting if they share their religion; they retain stoning; they do not consider children of disbelievers as disbelievers or eternally punished.
3
Understand their view on taqiyya
They permit taqiyya in speech but not in action. This is a moderate stance compared to other sects.
4
Analyze their sin classification and marriage ruling
Sins with hadd punishment label the person by the sin (e.g., thief) but not disbeliever; sins without hadd like abandoning prayer constitute disbelief. They also permit marriage to a believing woman from a disbeliever in the abode of taqiyya only.
This shows a nuanced approach to takfir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصفرية: أصحاب زياد بن الأصفر يخالفون الأزارقة في تكفير القعدة عن القتال إذا كانوا موافقين لهم في الدين، وفي إسقاط الرجم فإنهم لم يسقطوه، وفي أطفال الكفار أي لم يكفروا أطفالهم ولم يقولوا بتخليدهم في النار، ومنع التقية في القول أي جوزوا التقية في القول دون العمل، وقالوا: المعصية الموجبة للحد لا يسمى صاحبها إلا بها فيقال مثلا: سارق أو زان أو قاذف ولا يقال: كافر، وما لا حد فيه العظمة كترك الصلاة والصوم كفر، فيقال لصاحبه كافر. وقيل: تزوج المؤمنة أي المعتقدة لما هو دينهم من الكافر المخالف لهم في دار التقية دون دار العلانية.
Sufriyya: Followers of Ziyad ibn al-Asfar. They differ from the Azariqa in declaring disbelief (takfir) of those who sit out of fighting if they are in agreement with them in religion, and in dropping stoning (rajm) for they did not drop it, and regarding the children of disbelievers: i.e., they did not declare their children disbelievers nor did they say they are eternally in the Fire, and they prohibited taqiyya in speech, i.e., they permitted taqiyya in speech but not in action. And they said: A sin that necessitates a hadd punishment does not make its doer called anything but that (act); so one says, for example, 'thief' or 'adulterer' or 'slanderer' but not 'disbeliever.' But a sin that has no hadd punishment of greatness, like abandoning prayer and fasting, is disbelief, so its doer is called a disbeliever. And it was said: He may marry a believing woman, i.e., one who believes in their religion, from a disbeliever who opposes them, in the abode of taqiyya but not in the abode of openness.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage outlines the doctrines of the Sufriyya sub-sect. They disagreed with the Azariqa on several points: they did not declare as disbelievers those who abstain from fighting if they share their religion; they retained stoning; they did not consider children of disbelievers as disbelievers or condemned to Hell; they allowed taqiyya in speech but not action; they distinguished between sins that have hadd punishments (these label the person as sinner but not disbeliever) and sins without hadd like abandoning prayer/fasting (which are disbelief). They also permitted marriage to a believing woman in a place of taqiyya but not in open opposition.

Key Terms
الأصفرية
القعدة عن القتال
إسقاط الرجم
أطفال الكفار
التقية
المعصية الموجبة للحد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Sufriyya completely rejected takfir.
Correction: They only limited takfir to certain sins (like abandoning prayer) and did not apply it to sins that incur hadd punishments.

Checkpoint
According to the Sufriyya, how is a person who commits a sin that necessitates a hadd punishment labeled?
A) As a disbeliever
B) By the specific sin (e.g., thief, adulterer)
C) As a hypocrite
D) As a polytheist

Key Takeaway
The Sufriyya distinguished between sins that incur divine punishments and those that incur worldly hadd punishments, thereby refining the concept of takfir.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you immediately label yourself as a 'disbeliever' or 'hopeless', ignoring the distinction the Sufriyya made between types of sins? How might this attitude affect your repentance?
?
The Sufriyya permitted taqiyya in speech but not in action. In what situations have you compromised your faith through your actions (even while verbally affirming it)? What will you do to align your actions with your speech starting today?
?
You now know that the Sufriyya did not declare the children of disbelievers as disbelievers. Is there a person or group you've dismissed as beyond guidance, perhaps based on their background? How does this lesson challenge you to reconsider your judgment?

Core Beliefs of the Ibadiyya
General beliefs of the Ibadiyya sect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinctive doctrines of the Ibadiyya sect, including their views on takfir, iman, and the status of major sinners.

Core Idea
Ibadiyya rejects Sunni consensus by declaring 'Ali a disbeliever.

The Ibadiyya sect, originating from 'Abd ibn Ibad, holds several unique positions that set it apart from mainstream Islam. This passage outlines their core beliefs regarding the status of opponents, major sinners, and key theological issues. Understanding these views is crucial for recognizing the diversity within Islamic sects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the founder
The passage begins by naming the founder, 'Abd ibn Ibad. Make a note of this as the starting point of the sect.
The name 'Ibadiyya' is clearly derived from 'Ibad.
2
List the key doctrines
Read through the passage and list each distinct belief: status of opponents, marriage and spoils, testimony, major sin, capability, free will, end of the world, and takfir.
Notice the nuanced position on takfir: kufr ni'ma not kufr milla.
3
Understand the hesitations
The Ibadiyya hesitated on several issues. Find them: children of disbelievers, hypocrisy, sending messengers without miracles.
These hesitations show a degree of uncertainty within the sect.
4
Note the takfir of 'Ali
The last doctrine declares 'Ali and most Companions as disbelievers. This is a radical position that contrasts with Sunni views.
This is a key point of difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأباضية: هو عبد بن أباض. قالوا: مخالفونا من أهل القبلة كفار غير مشركين يجوز مناكحتهم وغنيمة أموالهم من سلاحهم وكراعهم حلال عند الحرب دون غيره، ودارهم دار الإسلام إلا معسكر سلطانهم. وقالوا تقبل شهادة مخالفيهم عليهم، ومرتكب الكبيرة موحد غير مؤمن بناء على أن الأعمال داخلة في الإيمان، والاستطاعة قبل الفعل، وفعل العبد مخلوق لله تعالى، ويفنى العالم كله بفناء أصل التكليف، ومرتكب الكبيرة كافر كفر نعمة لا ملة. وتوقفوا في تكفير أولاد الكفار وتعذيبهم، وتوقفوا في النفاق أهو شرك أم لا، وفي جواز بعثة رسول بلا دليل ومعجزة، وتكليف أتباعه فيما يوحى إليه أي ترددوا أن ذلك جائز أو لا. وكفروا علياً وأكثر الصحابة. وافترقوا فرقا أربعا: الأولى الحفصية: هو أبو حفص بن أبي المقدام زادوا على الأباضية أن بين الإيمان والشرك معرفة الله تعالى فإنها خصلة متوسطة بينهما، فمن عرف الله وكفر بما سواه من رسول أو جنة أو نار أو بارتكاب كبيرة فكافر لا مشرك. الثانية: اليزيدية: أصحاب يزيد بن أنيسة زادوا على الأباضية أن قالوا سيبعث نبي من العجم بكتاب يكتب في السماء ويترك عليه جملة واحدة، ويترك شريعة محمد إلى ملة الصابئة المذكورة في القرآن، وقالوا: أصحاب الحدود مشركون وكل ذنب شرك كبيرة كانت أو صغيرة. الثالثة: الحارثية أصحاب أبي الحارث الأباضي. خالفوا الأباضية في القدر أي كون أفعال العباد مخلوقة لله تعالى، وفي كون الاستطاعة قبل الفعل. الرابعة: القائلون بطاعة لا يراد بها الله أي زعموا أن العبد إذا أتى بما أمر به ولم يقصد الله كان ذلك طاعة.
Ibadiyya: He is 'Abd ibn Ibad. They said: Our opponents among the people of the qibla are disbelievers but not polytheists; it is permissible to marry them and to take as spoils their weapons and horses as lawful during war but not otherwise. Their abode is the abode of Islam except for the camp of their sultan. They said: The testimony of their opponents is accepted against them. The committer of a major sin is a monotheist but not a believer, on the basis that works are included in faith. Capability (istita'a) is before the act, and the act of the servant is created by Allah. The entire world will perish with the annihilation of the origin of taklif (obligation). The committer of a major sin is a disbeliever of the type of disbelief of ingratitude (kufr ni'ma) not of the religion (milla). They hesitated regarding takfir of children of disbelievers and their punishment, and they hesitated regarding hypocrisy whether it is shirk or not, and regarding the permissibility of sending a messenger without a proof and miracle, and imposing obligation upon his followers regarding what is revealed to him; i.e., they doubted whether that is permissible or not. They declared 'Ali and most of the Companions to be disbelievers. And they split into four groups: First: the Hafsiyya: He is Abu Hafs ibn Abi al-Miqdam; they added to the Ibadiyya that between faith and shirk is knowledge of Allah, for it is a middle characteristic between the two. So whoever knows Allah and disbelieves in everything else, whether a messenger, Paradise, Hell, or by committing a major sin, is a disbeliever, not a polytheist. Second: the Yazidiyya: Followers of Yazid ibn Anisa; they added to the Ibadiyya that they said: A prophet will be sent from the non-Arabs with a book that will be written in heaven and left upon it as a single whole, and the law of Muhammad will be abandoned for the religion of the Sabians mentioned in the Quran. And they said: The people of the prescribed punishments are polytheists, and every sin is shirk, whether major or minor. Third: the Harithiyya: Followers of Abu al-Harith al-Ibadi; they opposed the Ibadiyya regarding qadar, i.e., that the actions of servants are created by Allah, and regarding capability being before the act. Fourth: Those who say: obedience not intended for Allah; i.e., they claimed that if a servant does what he is commanded and does not intend Allah, that is obedience.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage comprehensively describes the Ibadiyya sect and its four sub-sects. The Ibadiyya held that opponents are disbelievers but not polytheists, allowing intermarriage and spoils only during war, accepting testimony of opponents, and distinguishing between kufr ni'ma and kufr milla. They had hesitations on children of disbelievers, hypocrisy, and sending prophets without miracles. They declared 'Ali and most Companions as disbelievers. They split into four: Hafsiyya inserted knowledge of Allah as an intermediate between faith and shirk; Yazidiyya predicted a future prophet from non-Arabs who will abrogate Muhammad's law to Sabianism and considered all sins as shirk; Harithiyya disagreed on qadar and istita'a; the fourth group held that obedience without intention is valid.

Key Terms
الأباضية
مخالفونا من أهل القبلة
كفار غير مشركين
مرتكب الكبيرة
الاستطاعة قبل الفعل
فعل العبد مخلوق
كفر نعمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ibadiyya completely rejected takfir.
Correction: Their takfir is limited to kufr ni'ma, but they still declared 'Ali a disbeliever.

Checkpoint
According to the Ibadiyya, what is the status of a committer of a major sin?
A) He is a polytheist
B) He is a monotheist but not a believer
C) He is a believer
D) He is a hypocrite

Key Takeaway
The Ibadiyya sect holds that major sinners are kafir in the sense of ingratitude, not unbelief, yet they declared 'Ali and many Companions as disbelievers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Ibadiyya declared 'Ali, a companion revered by Sunnis, a disbeliever. Is there any person or group you have dismissed from the fold of faith without proper knowledge? Will you commit to seeking understanding before judging?
?
The Ibadiyya defined major sinners as kafir in the sense of ingratitude, not unbelief. Have you ever treated a fellow Muslim's sin as a total rejection of Islam, forgetting that sin and disbelief are distinct? How can you show mercy while still upholding truth?
?
The Ibadiyya hesitated on certain matters like the punishment of children of disbelievers. Are you comfortable with ambiguity in theological questions, or do you rush to definitive stances? How can you balance certainty in core beliefs with humility on secondary issues?

The Four Sub-Sects of Ibadiyya
Enumeration of the four sub-sects of Ibadiyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four sub-sects of Ibadiyya: Hafsiyya, Yazidiyya, Harithiyya, and the group on obedience without intention.

Core Idea
Each Ibadi sub-sect added a unique twist on faith, prophethood, or free will.

After outlining general beliefs, the source enumerates four sub-sects that emerged from the Ibadiyya. Each group introduced a distinctive doctrine, ranging from the intermediate status of knowing Allah to the abrogation of Islamic law. This lesson breaks down their innovations.

Guided Path
1
Read the four groups
Read the passage listing the four sub-sects: Hafsiyya, Yazidiyya, Harithiyya, and the proponents of obedience without intention.
2
Compare each group's addition
For each sub-sect, identify what they added or changed from mainstream Ibadiyya.
Hafsiyya adds knowledge of Allah as intermediate; Yazidiyya predicts a future prophet; Harithiyya rejects qadar; the fourth group accepts obedience without intention.
3
Evaluate the significance
Consider how these additions affect their overall theology. For example, Yazidiyya's claim that all sins are shirk is radical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأباضية: هو عبد بن أباض. قالوا: مخالفونا من أهل القبلة كفار غير مشركين يجوز مناكحتهم وغنيمة أموالهم من سلاحهم وكراعهم حلال عند الحرب دون غيره، ودارهم دار الإسلام إلا معسكر سلطانهم. وقالوا تقبل شهادة مخالفيهم عليهم، ومرتكب الكبيرة موحد غير مؤمن بناء على أن الأعمال داخلة في الإيمان، والاستطاعة قبل الفعل، وفعل العبد مخلوق لله تعالى، ويفنى العالم كله بفناء أصل التكليف، ومرتكب الكبيرة كافر كفر نعمة لا ملة. وتوقفوا في تكفير أولاد الكفار وتعذيبهم، وتوقفوا في النفاق أهو شرك أم لا، وفي جواز بعثة رسول بلا دليل ومعجزة، وتكليف أتباعه فيما يوحى إليه أي ترددوا أن ذلك جائز أو لا. وكفروا علياً وأكثر الصحابة. وافترقوا فرقا أربعا: الأولى الحفصية: هو أبو حفص بن أبي المقدام زادوا على الأباضية أن بين الإيمان والشرك معرفة الله تعالى فإنها خصلة متوسطة بينهما، فمن عرف الله وكفر بما سواه من رسول أو جنة أو نار أو بارتكاب كبيرة فكافر لا مشرك. الثانية: اليزيدية: أصحاب يزيد بن أنيسة زادوا على الأباضية أن قالوا سيبعث نبي من العجم بكتاب يكتب في السماء ويترك عليه جملة واحدة، ويترك شريعة محمد إلى ملة الصابئة المذكورة في القرآن، وقالوا: أصحاب الحدود مشركون وكل ذنب شرك كبيرة كانت أو صغيرة. الثالثة: الحارثية أصحاب أبي الحارث الأباضي. خالفوا الأباضية في القدر أي كون أفعال العباد مخلوقة لله تعالى، وفي كون الاستطاعة قبل الفعل. الرابعة: القائلون بطاعة لا يراد بها الله أي زعموا أن العبد إذا أتى بما أمر به ولم يقصد الله كان ذلك طاعة.
Ibadiyya: He is 'Abd ibn Ibad. They said: Our opponents among the people of the qibla are disbelievers but not polytheists; it is permissible to marry them and to take as spoils their weapons and horses as lawful during war but not otherwise. The committer of a major sin is a disbeliever of the type of disbelief of ingratitude (kufr ni'ma) not of the religion (milla). Fourth: Those who say: obedience not intended for Allah; i.e., they claimed that if a servant does what he is commanded and does not intend Allah, that is obedience.

This passage comprehensively describes the Ibadiyya sect and its four sub-sects. The Ibadiyya held that opponents are disbelievers but not polytheists, allowing intermarriage and spoils only during war, accepting testimony of opponents, and distinguishing between kufr ni'ma and kufr milla. Checkpoint
Which sub-sect believed that all sins, major and minor, are shirk?
A) Hafsiyya
B) Yazidiyya
C) Harithiyya
D) Proponents of obedience without intention

Key Takeaway
The Ibadiyya split into four sub-sects each with a unique theological addition: Hafsiyya (knowledge as intermediate), Yazidiyya (future prophet, all sins shirk), Harithiyya (free will), and the fourth (obedience without intention).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Hafsiyya taught that knowing Allah while rejecting everything else makes one a disbeliever, not a polytheist. In your own life, do you ever separate your intellectual belief in Allah from obedience to His messengers and commands? What would it mean for you to truly submit to the whole of Islam, not just acknowledge God's existence?
?
The Yazidiyya expected a future prophet to replace the law of Muhammad. Have you ever felt tempted to follow a 'new', more convenient version of Islam that discards parts of the Sharia? Why do you think the Prophet (peace be upon him) is the final messenger, and how does that demand your exclusive loyalty today?
?
The Harithiyya disagreed with the majority on whether God creates human actions. When you sin, do you sometimes blame God's decree or feel trapped by fate? Examine one area of your life where you rely on excuses rather than taking responsibility. Will you, from this moment, own your choices and turn to Allah in repentance?

The Core Doctrines of the 'Ajarda Sect
Definition of 'Ajarda and its core doctrine of mandatory disavowal of children.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the defining beliefs of the 'Ajarda sect, especially their obligation to disavow children until they accept Islam after puberty and their judgment that children of polytheists go to Hell.

Core Idea
'Ajarda made disavowal of children mandatory and placed all polytheist children in the Fire.

The 'Ajarda, the seventh group of Khawarij, built on the Najdiyya but added a unique stance on children. They required believers to disavow children who have not yet professed Islam after reaching puberty, and they held that the children of polytheists are destined for Hell. This passage introduces these core doctrines before listing their ten sub-sects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on 'Ajarda's foundation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the main belief: obligatory disavowal of children until they profess Islam after puberty, and the fiery fate of polytheist children.
Notice the phrase 'وجوب البراءة عن الطفل'—this is the central tenet.
2
Identify the two doctrines
The passage presents two specific doctrines: (1) the obligation to disavow children and call them to Islam after puberty, and (2) that children of polytheists are in Hell. Make sure you can state each.
3
Reflect on the context
Consider how these doctrines relate to the broader Khawarij position on radical disavowal (bara'a) and judgment based on belief. How does this differ from mainstream Islam?
This passage sets the stage for the sub-sects that follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العجاردة: هو عبد الرحمن بن عجرد وهم آخر السبع من فرق الخوارج زادوا على النجدات بعد أن وافقوهم في مذهبهم وجوب البراءة عن الطفل أي يجب أن يتبرأ عنه حتى يدعي الإسلام بعد البلوغ ويجب دعاؤه إليه أي إلى الإسلام إذا بلغ، وأطفال المشركين في النار. وهم عشر فرق: الأولى: الميمونية: هو ميمون بن عمران قالوا بالقدر أي إسناد الأفعال إلى قدر العباد، ويكون الاستطاعة قبل الفعل، وأن الله يريد الخير دون الشر ولا يريد المعاصي كما هو مذهب المعتزلة، قالوا: وأطفال الكفار في الجنة، ويروى عنهم تجويز نكاح البنات للبنين وللبنات ولأولاد الإخوة والأخوات أي جوزوا نكاح بنات البنين وبنات البنات وبنات أولاد الإخوة والأخوات، وإنكار سورة يوسف فإنهم زعموا أنها قصة من القصص ولا يجوز أن تكون قصة الفسق قرآناً. الثانية: من فرق العجاردة والحمزية: هو حمزة بن أدرك، وافقوهم أي الميمونية فيما ذهبوا إليه من البدع إلا أنهم قالوا أطفال الكفار في النار. الثالثة منهم: الشعيبية: هو شعيب بن محمد وهم كالميمونية في بدعهم إلا في القدر. الرابعة: الحازمية هو حازم بن عاصم وافقوا الشعيبية ويحكى عنهم أنهم يتوقفون في أمر علي ولا يصرحون بالبراءة عنه كما يصرحون بالبراءة عن غيره. الخامسة: الخلفية: أصحاب خلف الخارجي وهم خوارج كرمان ومكران أضافوا القدر خيره وشره إلى الله وحكموا بأن أطفال المشركين في النار بلا عمل وشرك. السادسة: الأطرافية هم على مذهب حمزة ورئيسهم رجل من سجستان يقال له غالب إلا أنهم عذروا أهل الأطراف فيما لم يعرفوه من الشريعة إذا أتوا بما يعرف
'Ajarda: He is 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Ajrad. They are the last of the seven sects of the Khawarij. They added to the Najdiyya after agreeing with their school the obligation of disavowal (bara'a) of the child: i.e., one must disavow him until he professes Islam after puberty, and it is obligatory to call him to it, i.e., to Islam, when he reaches puberty. And the children of polytheists are in the Fire. They are ten sects: First: the Maymuniyya: He is Maymun ibn 'Imran. They held qadar (divine predestination), i.e., attributing actions to the power of servants, and that capability is before the act, and that Allah wills good not evil and does not will sins, as is the school of the Mu'tazila. They said: The children of disbelievers are in Paradise. It is narrated from them the permissibility of marrying daughters to sons, and to daughters, and to children of brothers and sisters, i.e., they permitted marriage of granddaughters and daughters of nieces/nephews, and the denial of Sura Yusuf, for they claimed it is a story from stories and it is not permissible for a story of lewdness to be Quran. Second: from the sub-sects of 'Ajarda is the Hamziyya: He is Hamza ibn Adrak. They agreed with the Maymuniyya in the innovations they adopted, except that they said the children of disbelievers are in the Fire. Third: the Shu'aybiyya: He is Shu'ayb ibn Muhammad, and they are like the Maymuniyya in their innovations except regarding qadar. Fourth: the Hazimiyya: He is Hazim ibn 'Asim. They agreed with the Shu'aybiyya, and it is narrated that they hesitated regarding 'Ali and did not explicitly declare disavowal of him as they declared disavowal of others. Fifth: the Khalafiyya: Followers of Khalaf al-Khariji, and they are the Khawarij of Kirman and Makran. They attributed qadar, its good and evil, to Allah, and judged that the children of polytheists are in the Fire without work or shirk. Sixth: the Atrafiyya: They follow the school of Hamza, and their leader is a man from Sijistan called Ghalib, except that they excused the people of the peripheries (atraf) for what they did not know of the Shari'a if they act according to what they know.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage describes the 'Ajarda sect, the seventh group of Khawarij. They emphasized disavowal of children until they profess Islam after puberty. They had ten sub-sects; six are detailed here. The Maymuniyya held Mu'tazili-like qadar, that children of disbelievers are in Paradise, permitted certain incestuous marriages, and denied Sura Yusuf. The Hamziyya agreed except they placed children of disbelievers in Hell. The Shu'aybiyya were like Maymuniyya except on qadar. The Hazimiyya hesitated on disavowing 'Ali. The Khalafiyya attributed all qadar to Allah and placed polytheist children in Hell. The Atrafiyya excused ignorance on the peripheries.

Key Terms
العجاردة
البراءة عن الطفل
أطفال المشركين في النار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the 'Ajarda, when must a child be disavowed?
A) From birth until he professes Islam after puberty
B) Only if he refuses Islam at puberty
C) Only if his parents are polytheists
D) Never, because children are innocent

Key Takeaway
The 'Ajarda sect required disavowal of children until they profess Islam after puberty and held that children of polytheists go to Hell.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear of a child from a non-Muslim family passing away, does your heart immediately lean toward assuming their damnation? How does this lesson’s specific statement about polytheist children challenge your inner assumptions, and what will you do to align your thoughts with God’s mercy?
?
The ʿAjarda made it an obligation to disavow children until they professed Islam. In your life, is there any person you have ‘disavowed’—held at a distance—because they have not yet embraced Islam? How will you replace that disavowal with the patient compassion of the Prophet (peace be upon him)?
?
Do you find it easy to pass absolute judgments about God’s treatment of others, like the ʿAjarda did? Identify one judgment you have made about someone’s destiny and repent from it today by acknowledging that only God knows the final state of any soul.

The Six Sub-Sects of the 'Ajarda
Enumeration of six 'Ajarda sub-sects with their distinctive doctrines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the six sub-sects of the 'Ajarda based on their specific doctrines regarding qadar, the fate of polytheist children, marriage, and other issues.

Core Idea
Maymuniyya, Hamziyya, Shu'aybiyya, Hazimiyya, Khalafiyya, and Atrafiyya each held distinct positions within the 'Ajarda framework.

The 'Ajarda split into ten sub-sects; this passage details six of them. Each sub-sect takes a different stance on qadar (divine predestination), the destiny of polytheist children, and other matters such as marriage and the denial of a Quranic sura. The Hamziyya, for example, agreed with the Maymuniyya except on the fate of children, while the Shu'aybiyya differed on qadar. Let's examine each one.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage listing the six sub-sects
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, focusing on the names of the sub-sects and the distinctive belief mentioned for each.
The passage begins with 'الأولى: الميمونية' and ends with 'السادسة: الأطرافية'.
2
Create a mental table of differences
For each sub-sect, note its position on qadar, the fate of polytheist children, and any unique doctrine (e.g., marriage, denial of Sura Yusuf, hesitancy about 'Ali).
The Maymuniyya and Shu'aybiyya differ on qadar; Hamziyya and Maymuniyya differ on children's fate.
3
Identify which sub-sect held which view on qadar
The Maymuniyya had a Mu'tazili-like qadar (actions from servants), the Shu'aybiyya did not hold that view, and the Khalafiyya attributed all qadar to Allah. Understand these distinctions.
4
Reflect on the variety within the 'Ajarda
Consider how these sub-sects demonstrate internal diversity despite common origins. This helps understand the complex history of the Khawarij.

العجاردة: هو عبد الرحمن بن عجرد وهم آخر السبع من فرق الخوارج زادوا على النجدات بعد أن وافقوهم في مذهبهم وجوب البراءة عن الطفل أي يجب أن يتبرأ عنه حتى يدعي الإسلام بعد البلوغ ويجب دعاؤه إليه أي إلى الإسلام إذا بلغ، وأطفال المشركين في النار. وهم عشر فرق: الأولى: الميمونية: هو ميمون بن عمران قالوا بالقدر أي إسناد الأفعال إلى قدر العباد، ويكون الاستطاعة قبل الفعل، وأن الله يريد الخير دون الشر ولا يريد المعاصي كما هو مذهب المعتزلة، قالوا: وأطفال الكفار في الجنة، ويروى عنهم تجويز نكاح البنات للبنين وللبنات ولأولاد الإخوة والأخوات أي جوزوا نكاح بنات البنين وبنات البنات وبنات أولاد الإخوة والأخوات، وإنكار سورة يوسف فإنهم زعموا أنها قصة من القصص ولا يجوز أن تكون قصة الفسق قرآناً. الثانية: من فرق العجاردة والحمزية: هو حمزة بن أدرك، وافقوهم أي الميمونية فيما ذهبوا إليه من البدع إلا أنهم قالوا أطفال الكفار في النار. الثالثة منهم: الشعيبية: هو شعيب بن محمد وهم كالميمونية في بدعهم إلا في القدر. الرابعة: الحازمية هو حازم بن عاصم وافقوا الشعيبية ويحكى عنهم أنهم يتوقفون في أمر علي ولا يصرحون بالبراءة عنه كما يصرحون بالبراءة عن غيره. الخامسة: الخلفية: أصحاب خلف الخارجي وهم خوارج كرمان ومكران أضافوا القدر خيره وشره إلى الله وحكموا بأن أطفال المشركين في النار بلا عمل وشرك. السادسة: الأطرافية هم على مذهب حمزة ورئيسهم رجل من سجستان يقال له غالب إلا أنهم عذروا أهل الأطراف فيما لم يعرفوه من الشريعة إذا أتوا بما يعرف

Misconception & Correction

?
The Maymuniyya denied Sura Yusuf because they thought it contained a story of lewdness. What does this tell you about the condition of your heart towards Allah's revelation?
?
The 'Ajarda sub-sects held strong views about the fate of children of disbelievers. Do you ever find yourself making judgments about people's eternal destiny based on your own assumptions rather than relying on clear texts? How can you cultivate humility in matters where Allah has not given you certainty?
?
The Atrafiyya excused people on the peripheries for their ignorance of the Shari'a. Are there areas of your own religious practice where you remain deliberately ignorant or accept shortcuts because 'you didn't know'? Will you commit today to seeking knowledge about one aspect of your faith that you have neglected?

The Four Early Kharijite Sub-Sects
Lists the four Kharijite sub-sects after the Ibadiyya with their distinctive beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinctive beliefs of the four early Kharijite sub-sects that split from the Ibadiyya.

Core Idea
The Kharijites fragmented into four sub-sects with divergent views on faith, predestination, and future prophethood.

After the initial Kharijite split, the Ibadiyya still produced sub-sects. This passage enumerates four that differed on key theological issues such as the nature of faith, the role of miracles, predestination, and the possibility of future prophethood. Understanding these sects clarifies the breadth of Kharijite thought and its internal disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall structure.
Notice the editorial parentheses in the Arabic – they are part of the scholarly formatting.
2
Identify the four sub-sects and their names
The passage lists four sects: al-Ḥafṣiyya, al-Yazīdiyya, al-Ḥārithiyya, and a fourth unnamed group. Note the founder or key figure associated with each.
3
For each sect, note the specific belief that distinguishes them
Each sect added or opposed a specific doctrine to the Ibadiyya: for al-Ḥafṣiyya it is the intermediate state of knowledge of God; for al-Yazīdiyya it is the future prophet and the view that all sins are polytheism; for al-Ḥārithiyya it is predestination and capacity; for the fourth, it is the definition of obedience.
Pay attention to the phrasing: 'zādū ʿalā al-ibāḍiyya' or 'khālafū al-ibāḍiyya'.
4
Reflect on the significance of these divergent views
Consider why these differences matter in Islamic theology. They show that early Kharijites were not monolithic but debated issues like the relationship between faith and works, the nature of prophethood, and human free will.
This connects to the misconception that all Kharijites held identical views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
توقفوا ( في النفاق أهو شرك ) أم لا، (و) في ( جواز بعثة رسول بلا دليل) ومعجزة ) وتكليف أتباعه ) فيما يوحى إليه أي ترددوا أن ذلك جائز أو لا ) وكفروا علياً وأكثر ، الصحابة وافترقوا) فرقا أربعا . ( الأولى الحفصية : هو أبو حفص بن أبي المقدام زادوا على الأباضية ( أن بين الإيمان والشرك معرفة الله تعالى ) فإنها خصلة متوسطة بينهما ( فمن عرف الله وكفر بما سواه من رسول أو جنة أو نار ) أو بارتكاب كبيرة فكافر لا مشرك . ( الثانية : اليزيدية : أصحاب يزيد بن أنيسة زادوا على الأباضية أن ( قالوا سيبعث نبي من العجم بكتاب يكتب في السماء ويترك عليه جملة واحدة ) ويترك شريعة محمد إلى ملة الصابئة ) المذكورة في القرآن (و) قالوا : ( أصحاب الحدود مشركون وكل ذنب شرك ) كبيرة كانت أو صغيرة ( الثالثة : الحارثية أصحاب أبي الحارث الأباضي. خالفوا الأباضية في القدر أي كون أفعال العباد مخلوقة لله تعالى ( وفي ) كون ( الاستطاعة قبل الفعل . الرابعة : القائلون بطاعة لا يراد بها الله ) أي زعموا أن العبد إذا أتى بما أمر به ولم يقصد الله كان ذلك طاعة .
They hesitated (regarding hypocrisy: is it polytheism) or not, and (regarding) the permissibility of sending a messenger without a miracle, and the obligation of his followers to believe in what is revealed to him, meaning they doubted whether that is permissible or not, and they declared 'Ali and most of the Companions as disbelievers, and they split into four sects. (First: al-Ḥafṣiyya: he is Abū Ḥafṣ ibn Abī al-Miqdām. They added to the Ibāḍiyya that between faith and polytheism is knowledge of God, for it is an intermediate trait between them. So whoever knows God and disbelieves in anything other than Him, whether a messenger or Paradise or Hell, or by committing a major sin, is a disbeliever, not a polytheist. (Second: al-Yazīdiyya: followers of Yazīd ibn Anīsa. They added to the Ibāḍiyya that they said a prophet will be sent from the non-Arabs with a book written in the sky and left as a single whole, and he will abandon the law of Muḥammad for the religion of the Ṣābi'ūn mentioned in the Qur'an. And they said: the people of the prescribed punishments are polytheists, and every sin is polytheism, whether major or minor. (Third: al-Ḥārithiyya: followers of Abū al-Ḥārith al-Ibāḍī. They opposed the Ibāḍiyya regarding predestination, i.e., that the actions of servants are created by God, and regarding the capacity being before the act. (Fourth: those who say obedience not intended for God, i.e., they claimed that if a servant does what he is commanded without intending God, that is obedience.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the first four sub-sects that emerged from the original Kharijite split after the Ibāḍiyya. The author begins by noting the issues that caused the split: hesitation over whether hypocrisy is polytheism, whether a messenger can be sent without a miracle, and whether followers must accept revelations without evidence. They declared 'Ali and most Companions disbelievers and split into four groups. The first, al-Ḥafṣiyya, added that knowledge of God is an intermediate state between faith and polytheism, so whoever knows God but disbelieves in anything else is a disbeliever but not a polytheist. The second, al-Yazīdiyya, claimed a future prophet from the non-Arabs would bring a book written in heaven and abrogate Muḥammad's law for the religion of the Ṣābi'ūn; they also held that all sins are polytheism. The third, al-Ḥārithiyya, opposed the Ibāḍiyya on predestination (that God creates actions) and that capacity exists before the act. The fourth held that obedience performed without intending God is still obedience. Each sect is defined by its distinctive addition or opposition to the Ibāḍiyya.

الخوارج
الأباضية
الحفصية
اليزيدية
الحارثية
القدر
الاستطاعة
الطاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Kharijites held identical views on faith and practice.
Correction: This passage shows internal diversity: on faith (al-Hafsiyya's intermediate state), on sin (al-Yazidiyya's view of all sins as polytheism), on predestination (al-Harithiyya), and on intention (fourth group). The Kharijites were not monolithic.

Checkpoint
Which of the four sub-sects taught that there is an intermediate state between faith and polytheism?
A) al-Yazīdiyya
B) al-Ḥafṣiyya
C) al-Ḥārithiyya
D) the fourth group

Key Takeaway
The early Kharijites fragmented into four sub-sects with distinct theological positions on faith, sin, predestination, and the definition of obedience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Hafsiyya said that knowing God but disbelieving in anything else makes you a disbeliever, not a polytheist. When you sin, do you treat that sin as a lesser offense than shirk, or do you excuse yourself by saying 'at least I know God'? Could that excuse be a veil hiding the reality of your disobedience?
?
The Yazidiyya believed every sin — even a small one — is polytheism. Think about a sin you committed recently, one you considered minor. If you truly believed it was shirk, would you still have done it? How would your attitude toward that sin change if you saw it as a form of associating partners with Allah?
?
The fourth sect said obedience without intention to please God is still obedience. Reflect on a good deed you performed recently: was your motive purely for Allah, or was there a trace of showing off or habit? Are you comfortable with the idea that your deeds might be accepted even if you didn't mean them for Him? What does that comfort — or discomfort — reveal about your heart?

The 'Ajārida Parent and First Three Sub-Sects
Introduces the 'Ajārida parent sect and enumerates the first three sub-sects (Maymūniyya, Hamziyya, Shu'aybiyya) with their key doctrines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational doctrines of the 'Ajārida sect and how the first three sub-sects diverged on issues of predestination and the fate of children.

Core Idea
The 'Ajārida split began with disagreements over predestination and children's afterlife.

The 'Ajārida are the last of the seven Kharijite groups, emerging from the Najdāt. Their distinctive doctrine was the obligation to disavow children until they reach puberty and embrace Islam. From this parent sect branched ten sub-sects, each with its own variations. This lesson introduces the parent sect and the first three sub-sects: al-Maymūniyya, al-Ḥamziyya, and al-Shu'aybiyya.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the parent sect
Note the definition of 'Ajārida and their core doctrine on children.
2
Identify the first sub-sect: al-Maymūniyya
See how they affirmed predestination in a Qadari sense, and held children of disbelievers in Paradise.
Also note their denial of Sūrat Yūsuf.
3
Compare the second and third sub-sects
Al-Ḥamziyya agreed except they put children in Hell. Al-Shu'aybiyya agreed except on predestination.
Observe how small changes create new sects.

( الخامسة : الخلفية : أصحاب خلف) الخارجي وهم خوارج كرمان ومكران ( أضافوا القدر خيره وشره إلى الله وحكموا بأن أطفال المشركين في النار بلا عمل وشرك . السادسة : الأطرافية ) هم على مذهب حمزة ورئيسهم رجل من سجستان يقال له : غالب إلا أنهم ( عذروا أهل الأطراف فيما لم يعرفوه من الشريعة) إذا أتوا بما يعرف لزومه من جهة العقل . ( ووافقوا أهل السنة في أصولهم وفي نفي القدر أي إسناد الأفعال إلى قدرة العبد وفي بعض النسخ وفي نفي القدرة أي نفي المقدرة المؤثرة عن العباد. (السابعة : المعلومية هم كالحازمية إلا أن المؤمن عندهم من عرف الله بجميع أسمائه وصفاته، ومن لم يعرفه كذلك فهو جاهل لا مؤمن ( وفعل العبد مخلوق لله تعالى . الثامنة : المجهولية : مذهبهم كمذهب الحازمية أيضاً إلا أنهم ( قالوا : يكفي معرفته تعالى ببعض أسمائه فمن علمه كذلك فهو عارف به مؤمن وفعل العبد مخلوق لله تعالى . ( التاسعة : الصلتية : هو عثمان بن أبي الصلت وقيل: بن الصامت هم كالعجاردة، لكن قالوا من أسلم واستجار بنا توليناه وبرئنا من أطفاله ) حتى يبلغوا فيدعوا إلى الإسلام فيقبلوا ، ( وروي عن بعضهم أن الأطفال ) سواء كانوا للمسلمين أو المشركين ( لا) ولاية لهم ولا عداوة ) حتى يبلغوا فيدعوا إلى الإسلام ويقبلوا أو ينكروا . ( العاشرة : ( من فرق العجاردة ( الثعالبة : هو ثعلب بن عامر قالوا بولاية الأطفال صغاراً كانوا أو كباراً حتى يظهر منهم إنكار الحق بعد البلوغ ( وقد نقل عنهم ) أيضاً ) أن الأطفال لا حكم لهم) من ولاية أو عداوة إلى أن يدركوا ، ( ويرون أخذ الزكاة من العبيد إذا استغنوا وإعطاءها لهم إذا افتقروا
al-'Ajārida: he is 'Abd al-Raḥmān ibn 'Ajrad, and they are the last of the seven (groups) of the Kharijite sects. They added to al-Najdāt, after agreeing with them in their doctrine, the obligation of disavowal of the child, i.e., one must disavow him until he claims Islam after reaching puberty, and it is obligatory to call him to it, i.e., to Islam, when he reaches puberty. And the children of the polytheists are in the Fire. And they are ten sects: First: al-Maymūniyya: he is Maymūn ibn 'Imrān. They affirmed predestination, i.e., attributing actions to the capacity of servants, and that capacity is before the act, and that God wills good not evil and does not will sins, as is the doctrine of the Mu'tazila. They said: the children of disbelievers are in Paradise, and it is related from them permitting marriage of daughters to sons and to daughters and to children of brothers and sisters, i.e., they permitted marriage of granddaughters and great-granddaughters and children of siblings. And they denied Sūrat Yūsuf, for they claimed it is a story of stories and it is not permissible for a story of immorality to be Qur'an. (Second: from the sects of al-'Ajārida) al-Ḥamziyya: he is Ḥamza ibn Adrak. They agreed with them, i.e., al-Maymūniyya, in the innovations they held, except that they said the children of disbelievers are in the Fire. (Third) among them: al-Shu'aybiyya: he is Shu'ayb ibn Muḥammad, and they are like al-Maymūniyya in their innovations except regarding predestination. (Fourth: al-Ḥāzimiyya: he is Ḥāzim ibn 'Āṣim. They agreed with al-Shu'aybiyya, and it is narrated from them that they suspend judgment concerning 'Alī and do not declare disavowal of him explicitly as they declare disavowal of others. (Fifth: al-Khalafiyya: followers of Khalaf al-Khārijī, and they are the Kharijites of Kirmān and Makrān. They attributed predestination, its good and evil, to God, and ruled that the children of polytheists are in the Fire without work or polytheism. (Sixth: al-Aṭrāfiyya: they follow the doctrine of Ḥamza, and their leader is a man from Sijistān called Ghālib, except that they excused the people of the frontiers for what they did not know of the law if they did what they knew to be necessary by reason. And they agreed with the Ahl al-Sunna in their principles and in negating predestination, i.e., attributing actions to the capacity of the servant, and in some copies 'negating power', i.e., negating effective power from servants. (Seventh: al-Ma'lūmiyya: they are like al-Ḥāzimiyya except that the believer according to them is one who knows God by all His names and attributes, and whoever does not know Him thus is ignorant, not a believer, and the action of the servant is created by God. (Eighth: al-Majhūliyya: their doctrine is like the doctrine of al-Ḥāzimiyya also, except that they said: knowledge of Him is sufficient by some of His names, so whoever knows Him thus is a knower of Him, a believer, and the action of the servant is created by God. (Ninth: al-Ṣaltiyya: he is 'Uthmān ibn Abī al-Ṣalt, and it is said ibn al-Ṣāmit. They are like al-'Ajārida, but they said: whoever becomes Muslim and seeks our protection, we befriend him and disavow his children until they reach puberty and are called to Islam and accept. And it is related from some of them that children, whether of Muslims or polytheists, have no friendship nor enmity until they reach puberty and are called to Islam and accept or reject. (Tenth: from the sects of al-'Ajārida) al-Tha'āliba: he is Tha'lab ibn 'Āmir. They affirmed friendship with children, young or old, until denial of the truth appears from them after puberty. And it is also transmitted from them that children have no ruling of friendship or enmity until they mature. And they hold taking zakāt from slaves if they become wealthy and giving it to them if they become poor.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage classifies the 'Ajārida, a major Kharijite branch that split from al-Najdāt, and enumerates its ten sub-sects. The author first defines the parent sect: they are the last of the seven Kharijite groups, and they added to al-Najdāt the obligation of disavowing children until they reach puberty and embrace Islam, and they held that polytheists' children are in Hell. Then he lists ten sub-sects: (1) al-Maymūniyya affirmed predestination and capacity before the act, denied that God wills evil, held children of disbelievers in Paradise, permitted certain marriages, and denied Sūrat Yūsuf. (2) al-Ḥamziyya agreed except they put children of disbelievers in Hell. (3) al-Shu'aybiyya agreed with al-Maymūniyya except on predestination. (4) al-Ḥāzimiyya agreed with al-Shu'aybiyya but suspended judgment on 'Alī. (5) al-Khalafiyya attributed predestination entirely to God and held children of polytheists in Hell. (6) al-Aṭrāfiyya followed Ḥamza but excused ignorance in frontier regions and agreed with Ahl al-Sunna on principles and denying human power. (7) al-Ma'lūmiyya required knowledge of all God's names for faith, and held actions created. (8) al-Majhūliyya required knowledge of only some names. (9) al-Ṣaltiyya disavowed children until they accept Islam, with some saying children have no status until maturity. (10) al-Tha'āliba affirmed friendship with children until they reject truth, and had rules on zakāt for slaves. Each sub-sect is defined by its specific addition or variation on these core issues.

Key Terms
العجاردة
الميمونية
الحمزية
الشعيبية
القدر
الاستطاعة
أطفال الكفار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All 'Ajārida sub-sects agreed on the fate of children.
Correction: The first three sub-sects already show disagreement: al-Maymūniyya said children of disbelievers are in Paradise, al-Ḥamziyya said they are in Hell, and al-Shu'aybiyya may have a different view.

Checkpoint
Which sub-sect of the 'Ajārida held that the children of disbelievers are in Paradise?
A) al-Ḥamziyya
B) al-Maymūniyya
C) al-Khalafiyya
D) al-Ṣaltiyya

Key Takeaway
The first three sub-sects of the 'Ajārida diverged mainly on predestination and the fate of children, illustrating how minor differences create new sects.

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
5 min
Sub-Sects 4–6: Hāzimiyya, Khalafiyya, and Aṭrāfiyya
Enumerates the fourth to sixth sub-sects of the 'Ajārida (Hāzimiyya, Khalafiyya, Aṭrāfiyya) with their distinctive doctrines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinctive doctrines of the fourth to sixth 'Ajārida sub-sects, especially regarding judgment on 'Ali, predestination, and excuse for ignorance.

Core Idea
The 'Ajārida branches further diverge on 'Ali, predestination extremes, and frontier excuse.

After the first three sub-sects focused on children and predestination, the next three introduce new issues: al-Ḥāzimiyya suspends judgment on 'Ali, al-Khalafiyya attributes all predestination to God, and al-Aṭrāfiyya excuses ignorance of the law on the frontiers. This lesson examines these three sub-sects in detail.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Ḥāzimiyya
Note their agreement with al-Shu'aybiyya and their unique position on 'Ali: they suspend judgment and do not explicitly disavow him.
2
Read about al-Khalafiyya
They attributed all predestination (good and evil) to God and held children of polytheists in Hell without work or polytheism.
This is a different predestination stance.
3
Read about al-Aṭrāfiyya
They followed Ḥamza's doctrine but excused people on the frontiers for ignorance of the law, and agreed with Ahl al-Sunna in negating predestination (attributing actions to the servant).
Note the textual variant 'negating power'.

Which sub-sect suspended judgment on 'Alī and did not explicitly disavow him?
A) al-Khalafiyya

Key Takeaway
The fourth to sixth sub-sects introduce new themes: suspension of judgment on 'Alī, total predestination, and excusing legal ignorance on frontiers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter someone you disagree with on religious matters, do you immediately disavow them, or do you exercise suspension of judgment as the Hāzimiyya did regarding 'Alī? What would it cost you to hold back a verdict on their faith?
?
The Khalafiyya believed children of polytheists are condemned without having done anything. Does this trouble your sense of justice? How do you reconcile God's mercy with this doctrine, and how does it affect the way you view non-Muslim families?
?
The Aṭrāfiyya excused ignorance of the law for frontier people. Are there areas of your own religious practice where you plead ignorance rather than seeking knowledge? What 'frontier' in your life have you been using as an excuse to remain complacent?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
