الفرقة الرابعة : من كبار الفرق الإسلامية المرجئة : لقبوا به لأنهم يرجئون العمل عن النية أي يؤخرونه في الرتبة عنها وعن الاعتقاد من أرجأه أي أخره ومنه أرجأه وآخاه أي أمهله وأخره، أو لأنهم يقولون : لا يضر مع الإيمان معصية كما لا ينفع مع الكفر طاعة فهم يعطون الرجاء ، وعلى هذا أن لا ينبغي يهمز لفظ المرجئة . وفرقهم خمس: اليونسية : هو يونس النميري قالوا : الإيمان هو المعرفة بالله والخضوع له والمحبة بالقلب فمن اجتمعت فيه هذه الصفات فهو مؤمن ولا يضر معها ترك الطاعات وارتكاب المعاصي ولا يعاقب عليها، وإبليس كان عارفاً بالله وإنما كفر باستکباره وترك الخضوع لله كما دل عليه قوله : أبى واستكبر وكان من الكافرين . العبيدية : أصحاب عبيد المكذب، زادوا على اليونسية أن علم الله لم يزل شيئاً غيره أي غير ذاته وكذا باقي صفاته، وأنه تعالى على صورة الإنسان لما ورد في الحديث من أن الله خلق آدم على صورة الرحمن. الغسانية : أصحاب غسان الكوفي قالوا الإيمان هو المعرفة بالله ورسوله وبما جاء من عندهما إجمالاً لا تفصيلاً، وهو أي الإيمان يزيد ولا ينقص وذلك الإجمال مثل أن يقول : قد فرض لله الحج ولا أدري أين الكعبة ولعلها بغير مكة وبعث محمداً، ولا أدري أهو الذي بالمدينة أم غيره وحرم الخنزير ولا أدري أهو هذه الشاة أم غيرها فإن القائل بهذه المقالات مؤمن ومقصودهم بما ذكروه أن هذه الأمور ليست داخلة في حقيقة الإيمان، وإلا فلا شبهة في أن عاقلاً لا يشك فيها . وغسان كان يحكيه أي القول بما ذهب إليه عن أبي حنيفة وبعده من المرجئة وهو افتراء عليه قصد به غسان ترويج مذهبه بموافقة رجل كبير مشهور، قال هذا فأصحاب المقالات قد عدوا أبا حنيفة وأصحابه من مرجئة أهل السنة، ولعل ذلك لأن المعتزلة في الصدر الأول كانوا يلقبون من خالفهم في القدر مرجئاً أو لأنه لما قال : الإيمان هو التصديق ولا يزيد ولا ينقص، ظن به الإرجاء بتأخير العمل عن الإيمان وليس كذلك إذا عرف منه المبالغة في العمل والاجتهاد فيه. الثوبانية : أصحاب ثوبان المرجئي. قالوا : الإيمان هو المعرفة والإقرار بالله وبرسله وبكل ما لا يجوز في العقل أن يفعله، وأما ما جاز في العقل أن يفعله فليس الاعتقاد به من الإيمان وأخروا العمل كله عن الإيمان ووافقهم على ذلك مروان بن غيلان وقيل : أبو مروان غيلان الدمشقي وأبو شمر ويونس بن عمران والفضل الرقاشي.
The fourth group: among the major Islamic sects, al-Murji'a: they were given this name because they defer (yurji'ūn) action from intention — i.e., they postpone it in rank from intention and from belief; from 'arja'ahu meaning 'he delayed it'; and from it [is] 'arja'ahu wa ākhāhu' meaning 'he gave him respite and delayed him'. Or because they say: disobedience does not harm with faith just as obedience does not benefit with disbelief, so they give hope. On this basis, the word 'al-Murji'a' should not be pronounced with a hamza. And their sub-sects are five: al-Yūnusiyya: he is Yūnus al-Numayrī; they said: faith is knowledge of Allah, humility before Him, and love in the heart; whoever combines these qualities is a believer, and abandoning acts of obedience and committing sins do not harm him, nor is he punished for them; and Iblis was a knower of Allah, but he disbelieved due to his arrogance and abandonment of humility before Allah, as indicated by His saying: 'He refused and was arrogant and was among the disbelievers' [al-Baqara 34]. Al-'Ubaydiyya: the companions of 'Ubayd al-Mukadhdhib; they added to al-Yūnusiyya that the knowledge of Allah has not ceased to be something other than Him — i.e., other than His essence — and likewise the rest of His attributes; and that He Almighty is in the form of a human, due to the hadith that Allah created Adam in the form of al-Rahman. Al-Ghassāniyya: the companions of Ghassān al-Kūfī; they said: faith is knowledge of Allah and His Messenger and of what came from them both in summary (ijmālan), not in detail — and it — i.e., faith — increases and does not decrease; and that summary is like saying: Allah has obligated Hajj, but I do not know where the Ka'ba is, perhaps it is other than Mecca; and Muhammad was sent, but I do not know if he is the one in Medina or another; and swine is forbidden, but I do not know if it is this sheep or another; for the one who says these statements is a believer. Their intent by what they mentioned is that these matters are not part of the reality of faith; otherwise, there is no doubt that a rational person would not doubt them. And Ghassān used to narrate — i.e., the statement he adopted — from Abū Ḥanīfa and later from the Murji'a, and it is a slander against him, intended by Ghassān to promote his own doctrine by the agreement of a great, famous man. He said this: the authors of doctrinal works have counted Abū Ḥanīfa and his companions among the Murji'a of Ahl al-Sunna; perhaps this is because the Mu'tazila in the early period used to label whoever opposed them on qadar as Murji', or because when he said 'faith is affirmation (taṣdīq) and does not increase or decrease,' they suspected him of irjā' by deferring action from faith, but it is not so, since his diligence in action and striving in it is known. Al-Thawbāniyya: the companions of Thawbān al-Murji'ī; they said: faith is knowledge and acknowledgment of Allah and His messengers and of everything whose doing is not permissible according to reason. As for what is permissible according to reason to do, belief in it is not part of faith; and they deferred all action from faith; and they were followed in this by Marwān ibn Ghaylān, and it is said: Abū Marwān Ghaylān al-Dimashqī, and Abū Shamr, and Yūnus ibn 'Imrān, and al-Faḍl al-Raqqāshī.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage defines the Murji'ah as a major Islamic sect, explains the etymology of their name, and details the beliefs of their sub-sects. The name 'Murji'a' derives from 'irjā'' meaning postponement, either because they defer action from intention in rank, or because they say sin does not harm with faith, giving hope (rajā'). The author notes that the word should not be pronounced with a hamza. The Murji'a sub-sects are five, but only four are described here (the fifth is presumably elsewhere). First, al-Yūnusiyya (Yūnus al-Numayrī) define faith as knowledge, humility, and love in the heart; acts do not affect faith or punishment, and Iblis is cited as an example of knowledge without humility. Second, al-'Ubaydiyya add to this that God's knowledge and attributes are distinct from His essence, and God is in human form (based on a hadith). Third, al-Ghassāniyya (Ghassān al-Kūfī) define faith as summary knowledge of God, His messenger, and revelation, without details; they cite bizarre examples of ignorance about specifics, yet still consider the person a believer, arguing these details are not part of faith's reality. The author comments that Ghassān falsely attributed his view to Abū Ḥanīfa to gain credibility, and explains why Abū Ḥanīfa was sometimes labeled as Murji' by the Mu'tazila due to his definition of faith as taṣdīq (affirmation) without increase or decrease, though this is a misunderstanding since Abū Ḥanīfa emphasized action. Finally, al-Thawbāniyya (Thawbān al-Murji'ī) define faith as knowledge and acknowledgment of God, messengers, and everything rationally necessary (i.e., what reason deems impossible to be done by God), while belief in matters permitted by reason is not part of faith; they defer all action from faith.

Key Terms
الثوبانية
الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Thawbāniyya, which of the following is NOT part of faith?
A) Knowledge of Allah
B) Belief in what reason deems impossible to do
C) Belief in what reason deems possible
D) Acknowledgment of the messengers

Key Takeaway
The Thawbāniyya limited faith to rationally necessary beliefs and deferred all actions from faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Thawbāniyya limited faith to what reason finds impossible to deny. But what about the things Allah asks you to believe that your mind cannot fully grasp—like the unseen realities of the afterlife? Do you truly submit to those, or do you secretly harbor doubts because they are not rationally necessary? Will you repent today for any hidden hesitation and ask Allah to increase your iman in the unseen?
?
This sect deferred all actions from faith. Think about your own life: do you ever act as if your deeds have no impact on your iman? Are there sins you commit lightly, thinking, 'My faith is still intact anyway'? If you believed that every action either strengthens or weakens your faith, what one specific change would you make in your daily routine starting today?
?
If you were to define faith using only what you consider rationally necessary, would your list match the Thawbāniyya's? Or would it be even smaller? What does that reveal about your reliance on your own intellect versus humble submission to revelation? Ask Allah to grant you the sincerity to believe in everything He has revealed, even if your reason does not demand it.

Counting the Kharijite Sects
Concluding note on the number of Kharijite sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the final tally of Kharijite sects is derived and the methodological principle that disallows arbitrary inclusion of subgroups.

Core Idea
Consistency in counting sects is essential; arbitrariness undermines the classification.

This passage wraps up the detailed enumeration of Kharijite subgroups. It gives the final numbers—nineteen or twenty-two—depending on which groups are considered, and warns against picking and choosing arbitrarily. Understanding this helps you see how later scholars systematized early sectarian divisions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic text
Read the Arabic passage slowly. Notice the key terms: الثعالبة, العجاردة, الأباضية. The text is concise and numerical.
This is a concluding summary, so it assumes prior knowledge of the subgroups.
2
Identify the two counts
The passage gives two possible totals: 19 sects (Tha'aliba only) or 22 sects (Tha'aliba + Ibadiyya). Mark where each number appears.
The first count excludes Ibadiyya, the second includes them.
3
Understand the methodological criticism
The author says counting one group but not the other is 'pure arbitrariness' (تحكم محض). Reflect on why this is a logical error.
This critique emphasizes that classifications must be based on consistent criteria, not personal preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة للمرصد الرابع. الثعالبة عاشرة أقسام العجاردة مع فرقها الأربع بل يكتفى عنها بهذه الأربع فتكون الفرق حينئذ تسع عشرة، وأيضاً إذا اعتبر فرق الأباضية وفرق الثعالبة معاً كانت الفرق كلها اثنتين وعشرين واعتبار إحدى الأربعين دون الأخرى تحكم محض.
Conclusion of the Fourth Observatory. The Tha'aliba are the tenth division of the 'Ajarda with their four subgroups, but they suffice with these four, so the sects then become nineteen. Also, if the sects of the Ibadiyya and the Tha'aliba are considered together, all the sects become twenty-two. Considering one of the two groups without the other is pure arbitrariness.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is a concluding note on the number of Kharijite sects. The author first states that the Tha'aliba are the tenth division of the 'Ajarda, having four subgroups. He notes that they are satisfied with these four, bringing the total number of sects to nineteen. He then adds that if one also considers the Ibadiyya and Tha'aliba together, the total becomes twenty-two. He criticizes any approach that counts one group while ignoring another as pure arbitrariness.

العجاردة
الأباضية

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage shows that inconsistency leads to flawed conclusions. Reflect on an area of your life where you have been inconsistent in applying principles. What step will you take today to align your actions with your stated beliefs?
?
The author insists on considering all relevant groups together. In your relationships, have you been guilty of giving weight to some opinions while ignoring others arbitrarily? Ask yourself: Whom am I excluding from consideration without justification?

The Murji'ah: Definition and Core Belief
Definition of the Murji'ah with naming reasons and core belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the term Murji'ah, the two reasons for their naming, and their core belief about faith and actions.

Core Idea
The Murji'ah postpone actions in rank, giving hope to believers.

Sanusi introduces the fourth major Islamic sect, the Murji'ah. He explains the linguistic origin of their name and the doctrinal reason for it. This passage sets the stage for understanding their position on faith and works.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own words come through before interpreting.
Notice the parentheses – they likely indicate quotations or editorial additions.
2
Identify the two naming reasons
The passage gives two reasons for the name Murji'ah. Find both: one linguistic, one doctrinal.
The linguistic reason is about postponing actions in rank; the doctrinal reason is about sin not harming faith.
3
Understand the doctrinal implication
The second reason says sin does not harm with faith. Consider what this means for the relationship between faith and deeds.
This is a key difference from other sects that emphasize the necessity of both.
4
Note the pronunciation rule
The author states the word 'al-Murji'ah' should not be pronounced with a hamza. This is a linguistic note.
5
Recognize the subsects
The passage ends by mentioning that there are five subsects of the Murji'ah. This tells us the topic is broader than just one group.
This prepares us for further details in later passages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرقة الرابعة : ( من كبار الفرق الإسلامية ( المرجئة : لقبوا به لأنهم يرجئون العمل عن النية ) أي يؤخرونه في الرتبة عنها وعن الاعتقاد من أرجأه أي أخره ومنه أرجأه وآخاه أي أمهله وأخره ، ( أو لأنهم يقولون : لا يضر مع الإيمان معصية) كما لا ينفع مع الكفر طاعة ( فهم يعطون الرجاء ) وعلى هذا أن لا ينبغي يهمز لفظ المرجئة ) وفرقهم خمس:
The Fourth Group among the Major Islamic Sects: the Murji'ah. They are named because they postpone actions relative to intention, i.e., they delay it in rank relative to intention and belief, from 'arja'a' meaning to delay. Or because they say: sin does not harm with faith, just as obedience does not benefit with disbelief; so they give hope. Accordingly, the word 'al-Murji'ah' should not be pronounced with a hamza. And their sects are five:
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the Murji'ah. It first states that they are the fourth major Islamic sect. It gives two reasons for their name: either because they postpone actions relative to intention and belief, explaining the linguistic root, or because they say that sin does not harm faith and obedience does not benefit disbelief, thus giving hope to believers. It then notes a phonological rule: the word should not be pronounced with a hamza. Finally, it mentions that they have five subsects.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Murji'ah completely exclude actions from faith.
Correction: The passage shows they merely postpone actions in rank, not that actions are irrelevant.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Murji'ah are named for postponing actions in rank, and their core belief is that sin does not harm faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The Murji'ah gave hope to sinners. But is your hope in Allah's mercy leading you to obedience or to complacency? Examine your heart: do you use hope as a license to sin or as motivation to strive?

Beliefs of the Yunusiyya Subsect
Describes the Yunusiyya subsect's definition of faith and the Iblis example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Yunusiyya definition of faith and its three inner components, and why they consider Iblis a disbeliever despite his knowledge.

Core Idea
Faith is inner knowledge, humility, and love—actions don't matter.

The Yunusiyya are a subsect of the Murji'ah who deeply internalize the idea that faith is a matter of the heart, not outward deeds. Their view is bold: even Iblis had knowledge of God, but lacked humility and love, so he was a disbeliever. This passage presents their core teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the Source Passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the compact definition of faith and the supporting Quranic verse.
The Arabic uses 'اليونسية' to name the sect.
2
Identify the Three Components of Faith
The Yunusiyya define faith as three things: knowledge of God (المعرفة بالله), humility before Him (الخضوع له), and love in the heart (المحبة بالقلب). Mark these in the text.
3
Understand the Exclusivity of Inner Faith
The passage states that whoever possesses these three qualities is a believer, even if they neglect duties or commit sins. This reflects the Murji'ah position that actions do not affect faith.
This is a key difference from other Muslim groups.
4
Examine the Case of Iblis
The Yunusiyya use Iblis as proof: he knew God (was عارفاً بالله) but disbelieved because of arrogance and lack of humility. This shows that knowledge alone is insufficient for faith.
They cite Quran 2:34 as evidence.
5
Reflect on the Implication
Consider how this definition affects the understanding of who is a believer. Does it make faith too easy to achieve? How does it differ from the mainstream view that faith includes actions?
This connects to broader theological debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اليونسية : هو يونس النميري قالوا : الإيمان ) هو ( المعرفة بالله والخضوع له والمحبة بالقلب ) فمن اجتمعت فيه هذه الصفات فهو مؤمن ) ولا يضر معها ترك الطاعات ) وارتكاب المعاصي ولا يعاقب عليها ، ( وإبليس كان عارفاً بالله وإنما كفر باستکباره وترك الخضوع لله كما دل عليه قوله : أبى واستكبر وكان من الكافرين ﴾ [البقرة : ٣٤]
The Yunusiyya: They are followers of Yunus al-Numayri. They said: Faith is knowledge of God, humility before Him, and love in the heart. Whoever possesses these qualities is a believer; neglect of acts of obedience and commission of sins do not harm him, and he will not be punished for them. And Iblis knew God but disbelieved due to his arrogance and abandonment of humility before God, as indicated by His saying: 'He refused and was arrogant, and he was among the disbelievers' (Quran 2:34).
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage describes the Yunusiyya subsect. It states that their founder is Yunus al-Numayri. They define faith as three inner qualities: knowledge of God, humility before Him, and love in the heart. Whoever has these is a believer regardless of outward actions. They cite Iblis as an example: he had knowledge of God but disbelieved due to pride and lack of humility, as supported by the Quranic verse.

Key Terms
اليونسية
الإيمان
المعرفة
الخضوع
المحبة
إبليس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Yunusiyya consider mere intellectual knowledge of God sufficient for faith.
Correction: They require not just knowledge but also humility and love. Iblis is the counterexample: he had knowledge but lacked humility, so he was not a believer.

Checkpoint
According to the Yunusiyya, why did Iblis disbelieve despite knowing God?
A) He lacked knowledge.
B) He was arrogant and lacked humility.
C) He committed a sin.
D) He denied God's existence.

Key Takeaway
The Yunusiyya define faith solely as inner knowledge, humility, and love, making Iblis a disbeliever because he lacked humility despite knowing God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to examine your own heart right now, do you possess true knowledge of God, genuine humility, and sincere love? And if not, which one is lacking, and what will you do today to cultivate it?
?
The Yunusiyya taught that sins do not harm one's faith as long as these inner qualities are present. But do you ever use excuses—'I know God, I love Him'—to justify disobedience? How can you change that pattern starting now?
?
Iblis knew God intimately yet fell due to arrogance. Where in your life have you been content with mere knowledge without the humility to act on it? Commit to one concrete step this week to act in humility despite your knowledge.

The 'Ubaydiyya: Divine Attributes and Anthropomorphism
Enumerates the added beliefs of the 'Ubaydiyya subsect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two distinctive doctrines added by the 'Ubaydiyya subsect: that God's attributes are distinct from His essence and that God is in human form, based on a hadith.

Core Idea
The 'Ubaydiyya believed God's attributes are other than His essence and that He is in human form.

This lesson introduces the 'Ubaydiyya subsect, an offshoot of the Murji'ah. They built upon the Yunusiyya by adding two controversial beliefs about God's attributes and form. Understanding these additions helps clarify the spectrum of early Islamic theological positions on divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note that it describes the 'Ubaydiyya as followers of 'Ubayd al-Mukadhdhib and lists their additions to the Yunusiyya.
The passage is concise; each phrase carries doctrinal weight.
2
Identify the two added beliefs
The passage states two beliefs: (1) God's knowledge and other attributes are something other than His essence, and (2) God is in the form of a human, citing a hadith. Identify each in the text.
The first belief is about attribute realism; the second involves anthropomorphism.
3
Understand the hadith reference
The hadith 'God created Adam in the form of the Most Merciful' is used by the 'Ubaydiyya to support their view. Reflect on how scripture can be interpreted literally or figuratively.
Other sects interpret this hadith differently, avoiding anthropomorphism.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why these additions were seen as extreme. How do they contrast with mainstream Sunni views on divine transcendence and attribute distinction?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العبيدية : أصحاب عبيد المكذب، زادوا على اليونسية ( أن علم الله لم يزل شيئاً غيره أي غير ذاته وكذا باقي صفاته ( وأنه تعالى على ) صورة الإنسان لما ورد في الحديث من أن الله خلق آدم على صورة الرحمن.
The 'Ubaydiyya: The followers of 'Ubayd al-Mukadhdhib. They added to the Yunusiyya that God's knowledge has not ceased to be something other than Him, i.e., other than His essence, and similarly the rest of His attributes, and that He, exalted is He, is in the form of a human, due to the hadith that God created Adam in the form of the Most Merciful.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage describes the 'Ubaydiyya subsect. They are followers of 'Ubayd al-Mukadhdhib. They build upon the Yunusiyya by adding two specific doctrines: first, that God's knowledge and other attributes are distinct from His essence (a form of divine attribute realism); second, that God is in the form of a human, citing the hadith that God created Adam in His form (often interpreted as the form of the Most Merciful).

Key Terms
العبيدية
علم الله
الصفات
صورة الإنسان
حديث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the 'Ubaydiyya believed in pure anthropomorphism without scriptural basis.
Correction: The 'Ubaydiyya specifically based their anthropomorphic view on a hadith: 'God created Adam in the form of the Most Merciful.'

Checkpoint
What did the 'Ubaydiyya add to the Yunusiyya belief regarding God's attributes?
A) Attributes are identical to essence.
B) God's attributes are distinct from His essence.
C) Attributes are created.
D) God has no attributes.

Key Takeaway
The 'Ubaydiyya subsect held two distinctive views: divine attributes as separate from essence and God in human form, the latter based on a specific hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God, do you ever catch yourself forming a mental image, even vague? This lesson shows how some sects fell into literal anthropomorphism from a hadith. What specific step can you take this week to purify your belief about God's nature?
?
The 'Ubaydiyya treated God's attributes as separate from His essence. Have you ever treated one of God's attributes—like His mercy or justice—as a detached concept rather than a reality that shapes your daily actions? What would change if you truly internalized that His attributes are inseparable from who He is?
?
This passage reveals that even within the Murji'ah, there were serious deviations. Examine your own circle: are there any beliefs you hold about God that might be based on a literal reading of a text without considering mainstream scholarly interpretation? What is one specific belief you need to re-examine today?

Belief of the Ghassaniyya on Faith
Ghassaniyya define faith as general knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ghassaniyya's definition of faith as general knowledge and why they considered detailed knowledge not essential.

Core Idea
Faith according to Ghassaniyya is general knowledge, not detailed.

The Ghassaniyya were a sect that defined faith in a minimalistic way. They argued that a person could be ignorant of specific details of religion yet still be a believer. This lesson examines their position and the absurd examples they used.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its English translation. Notice the definition and examples.
The examples are deliberately extreme.
2
Identify the definition and examples
Find the statement defining faith and list the three examples they give to illustrate 'general knowledge'.
3
Reflect on the rationale
Consider why the Ghassaniyya claim such ignorance does not negate faith. What is their underlying intention?
They aim to show that these details are not part of the reality of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الغسانية : أصحاب غسان الكوفي قالوا الإيمان ) هو ( المعرفة بالله ورسوله وبما جاء من عندهما إجمالاً ) لا تفصيلاً ) وهو) أي الإيمان ( يزيد ولا ينقص وذلك ) الإجمال (مثل أن يقول : قد فرض لله الحج ولا أدري أين الكعبة ولعلها بغير مكة وبعث محمداً، ولا أدري أهو الذي بالمدينة أم غيره ) وحرم الخنزير ولا أدري أهو هذه الشاة أم غيرها فإن القائل بهذه المقالات مؤمن ومقصودهم بما ذكروه أن هذه الأمور ليست داخلة في حقيقة الإيمان، وإلا فلا شبهة في أن عاقلاً لا يشك فيها ( وغسان كان يحكيه أي القول بما ذهب إليه ( عن أبي حنيفة ) وبعده من المرجئة ( وهو افتراء علیه قصد به غسان ترويج مذهبه بموافقة رجل كبير مشهور، قال هذا فأصحاب المقالات قد عدوا أبا حنيفة وأصحابه من مرجئة أهل السنة، ولعل ذلك لأن المعتزلة في الصدر الأول كانوا يلقبون من خالفهم في القدر مرجئاً أو لأنه لما قال : الإيمان هو التصديق ولا يزيد ولا ينقص، ظن به الإرجاء بتأخير العمل عن الإيمان وليس كذلك إذا عرف منه المبالغة في العمل والاجتهاد فيه.
The Ghassaniyya: The followers of Ghassan al-Kufi. They said: Faith is knowledge of God and His Messenger and of what came from them in general, not in detail. It increases and decreases. The general [knowledge] is like saying: God has prescribed Hajj, but I do not know where the Kaaba is; perhaps it is not in Mecca. And He sent Muhammad, but I do not know if he is the one in Medina or another. And He forbade swine but I do not know if it is this sheep or another. Indeed, the one who holds these views is a believer. Their intention by what they mentioned is that these matters are not part of the reality of faith. Otherwise, there is no doubt that a rational person would not doubt them. And Ghassan used to attribute this statement to Abu Hanifa, and after him to the Murji'ah, but it is slander against him, intended by Ghassan to popularize his own school by claiming agreement with a great and famous man. So [scholars] said: The authors of the articles have counted Abu Hanifa and his companions among the Murji'ah of Ahl al-Sunnah. Perhaps that is because the Mu'tazila in the early period used to call anyone who disagreed with them on Qadr a Murji', or because he said: Faith is affirmation and does not increase or decrease, so he was suspected of irja' by delaying action from faith, but that is not the case, for he is known for his extreme devotion to action and effort in it.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage describes the Ghassaniyya subsect and then discusses the false attribution of their views to Abu Hanifa. The Ghassaniyya define faith as general knowledge of God and His Messenger, not detailed. They illustrate this with absurd examples like not knowing the location of the Kaaba or the identity of the Prophet, yet claiming the person is still a believer. Their point is that such details are not part of faith. The author then notes that Ghassan falsely attributed this view to Abu Hanifa and the Murji'ah to gain credibility. The author defends Abu Hanifa, explaining that some scholars counted him among the Murji'ah due to the Mu'tazila's polemical labeling or because of his definition of faith as affirmation (tasdiq) without increase or decrease. However, the author clarifies that Abu Hanifa was extremely diligent in practice, so his view does not imply the neglect of actions.

Key Terms
الغسانية
الإيمان
المعرفة
الإجمال
التفصيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Ghassaniyya required no knowledge at all for faith.
Correction: The passage shows they require general knowledge, just not detailed.

Checkpoint
According to the Ghassaniyya, what is faith?
A) Detailed knowledge of all religious matters
B) General knowledge of God and His Messenger
C) Performance of all religious duties
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The Ghassaniyya define faith as mere general knowledge, not requiring detailed belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You acknowledge the obligation of Hajj, but when was the last time you actively learned about its rituals? Are you content with just general knowledge, or does your faith compel you to seek details? What one step will you take today to move from general acceptance to detailed understanding?
?
You claim to believe in the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), but do you truly know him—his character, his sacrifices, his teachings? Or is your 'belief' merely a label? If you were tested on your detailed knowledge of his life, would you pass? Commit to reading his biography this month.
?
The Ghassaniyya said a person ignorant of where the Kaaba is can still be a believer. You do know where it is. Do you long for it? Does your heart ache to stand before it? Your knowledge is detailed, but is your love? What will you sacrifice this year to turn your knowledge into longing?

Defending Abu Hanifa from False Attribution
Defense of Abu Hanifa from slander by Ghassan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the false attribution of the Ghassaniyya view to Abu Hanifa and the reasons behind it.

Core Idea
Ghassan's attribution of his view to Abu Hanifa was slander to gain credibility.

The Ghassaniyya's founder Ghassan claimed that his view on faith was also held by Abu Hanifa and the Murji'ah. However, this is revealed to be slander. This lesson explores the motives and the defense of Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on the claim and its refutation.
Notice the author's strong language: 'وهو افتراء عليه'.
2
Understand the claim and its refutation
Identify that Ghassan attributed his view to Abu Hanifa to popularize his school. The author calls it slander.
3
Analyze why Abu Hanifa was sometimes called Murji'
Consider the two possible reasons given: (1) Mu'tazila polemics regarding Qadr, (2) Abu Hanifa's definition of faith as affirmation without increase/decrease.
The author defends Abu Hanifa by noting his extreme devotion to practice.

Source Text

The general [knowledge] is like saying: God has prescribed Hajj, but I do not know where the Kaaba is; perhaps it is not in Mecca. A) Because Abu Hanifa actually held that view.

?

?

?
The Mu'tazila labeled their opponents as Murji'ah to discredit them. Are there people you disagree with religiously whom you have unfairly labeled or dismissed? How can you instead seek to understand their actual positions, as the author did for Abu Hanifa?

Thawbaniyya: Definition of Faith
Definition of faith by Thawbaniyya with followers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Thawbaniyya definition of faith as knowledge and acknowledgment of what is rationally impossible for God, and their postponement of actions.

Core Idea
Faith is knowledge and acknowledgment of the impossible, not of the possible.

The Thawbaniyya subsect, followers of Thawban al-Murji'i, had a unique definition of faith that set them apart. They restricted belief to matters that are rationally impossible for God, while excluding actions and matters rationally possible. This passage introduces their view and lists several prominent followers.

Guided Path
1
Read the faith definition
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice how the Thawbaniyya define faith: as knowledge and acknowledgment (ma'rifa wa iqrar) of God, His messengers, and everything that is rationally impossible for God to do.
They contrast this with what is rationally possible for God, which they exclude from faith.
2
Identify what is excluded
Understand that matters which are rationally possible for God (e.g., forgiving or punishing) are not part of faith according to them. Also, all actions are postponed (irja') from faith.
This shows their Murji'i inclination.
3
Note the followers
The passage lists several individuals who agreed with this view: Marwan ibn Ghilan (or Abu Marwan Ghilan al-Dimashqi), Abu Shamr, Yunus ibn 'Imran, and al-Fadl al-Raqqashi.
Ibn Ghilan later held additional views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثوبانية : أصحاب ثوبان المرجئي. قالوا : الإيمان هو المعرفة والإقرار بالله وبرسله وبكل ما لا يجوز في العقل أن يفعله، وأما ما جاز في العقل أن يفعله فليس الاعتقاد به من الإيمان وأخروا العمل كله عن الإيمان ووافقهم على ذلك مروان بن غيلان وقيل : أبو مروان غيلان الدمشقي وأبو شمر ويونس بن عمران والفضل الرقاشي ( و ) هؤلاء كلهم ( اتفقوا على أنه تعالى لو عفا ) في القيامة ( عن عاص لعفا عن كل من هو مثله وكذا لو أخرج واحداً من (النار لأخرج كل من هو مثله ( ولم يجزموا بخروج المؤمنين من النار، واختص ابن غيلان أو ( غيلان ) من بينهم (بالقدر)، إذ قد جمع بين الإرجاء والقول بالقدر أي إسناد الأفعال إلى العباد ( والخروج) من حيث أنه قال : يجوز أن لا يكون الإمام قرشيا
The Thawbaniyya: The followers of Thawban al-Murji'i. They said: Faith is knowledge and acknowledgment of God and His messengers and of everything that is not rationally impossible for Him to do. As for what is rationally possible for Him to do, belief in it is not part of faith. They postponed all actions from faith. They were agreed upon by Marwan ibn Ghilan, and it is said Abu Marwan Ghilan al-Dimashqi, and Abu Shamr, and Yunus ibn 'Imran, and al-Fadl al-Raqqashi. And all of them agreed that if He, exalted, were to forgive a sinner in the Hereafter, He would forgive everyone like him, and similarly if He were to remove one from the Fire, He would remove everyone like him. They did not definitively affirm the exit of believers from the Fire. And Ibn Ghilan, or Ghilan, was distinguished among them by [belief in] Qadr, as he combined irja' with Qadr, i.e., attributing actions to servants, and by [the opinion] that the imam need not be from Quraysh.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage describes the Thawbaniyya subsect. They define faith as knowledge and acknowledgment of God, His messengers, and matters that are rationally impossible for God to do (like lying). Matters that are rationally possible are not part of faith. They completely postpone actions from faith. The passage lists several followers, including Marwan ibn Ghilan and others. These followers all agreed on a particular view of God's forgiveness: if God were to forgive a sinner, He would forgive all similar sinners, and similarly if He removes one from the Fire, He removes all like him. They did not affirm definitively that any believers would exit the Fire. Ibn Ghilan is singled out for his belief in Qadr (human free will) and the opinion that the imam does not necessarily have to be from Quraysh, combining irja' with Qadar.

Key Terms
الثوبانية
المعرفة
الإقرار
الإرجاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Thawbaniyya believed that faith includes belief in everything about God, including what He might do (like forgiving).
Correction: They explicitly exclude belief in matters that are rationally possible for God from the definition of faith.

Checkpoint
According to the Thawbaniyya, what is part of faith?
A) Belief in all actions commanded by God
B) Knowledge and acknowledgment of God, His messengers, and what is rationally impossible for God
C) Belief that God will forgive sinners
D) Performing religious obligations

Key Takeaway
The Thawbaniyya defined faith narrowly as knowledge and acknowledgment of what is rationally impossible for God, excluding actions and matters of divine possibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your own iman, do you find yourself acting as if only your knowledge and acknowledgment matter, while obedience is optional? What specific act of worship have you been postponing because you thought your belief alone was enough?
?
The Thawbaniyya limited faith to what is rationally impossible for God. Are there areas of God's decree (qadr) that you struggle to submit to because they are 'possible' in your mind? What must you do to submit wholeheartedly to whatever He wills, even if it seems harsh?
?
Acknowledgment (iqrar) requires more than inner conviction. Do your words and actions publicly acknowledge God in every situation? What is one place in your life where your acknowledgment is only private, and how can you make it public?

Thawbaniyya on Divine Forgiveness
Thawbaniyya agreement on conditional forgiveness and non-affirmation of exit from Fire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Thawbaniyya's hypothetical view that if God forgives one sinner, He must forgive all similar sinners, and their refusal to definitively affirm the exit of believers from the Fire.

Core Idea
If God forgives one sinner, He must forgive all similar sinners.

The Thawbaniyya held a distinctive view on divine mercy: if God were to forgive a single sinner, He would be compelled to forgive all those in the same state. They also refrained from affirming that any believers would exit the Fire. This lesson explores their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the forgiveness passage
Read the Arabic passage on forgiveness. It says all the listed followers agreed on a conditional universalism: if God forgives a sinner, He forgives everyone like him; if He removes one from the Fire, He removes all like him.
This is a hypothetical statement, not a definite affirmation.
2
Understand the logic
The Thawbaniyya believed God's justice or mercy is uniform. They did not think God could treat two similar cases differently without contradiction.
This is similar to some Mu'tazili reasoning.
3
Note their agnosticism
Despite this hypothetical, they did not definitively affirm that any believers would actually exit the Fire. This shows caution or perhaps a Murji'i tendency to leave judgment to God.
They say 'lam yajzimū' (did not definitively affirm).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثوبانية : أصحاب ثوبان المرجئي. قالوا : الإيمان هو المعرفة والإقرار بالله وبرسله وبكل ما لا يجوز في العقل أن يفعله، وأما ما جاز في العقل أن يفعله فليس الاعتقاد به من الإيمان وأخروا العمل كله عن الإيمان ووافقهم على ذلك مروان بن غيلان وقيل : أبو مروان غيلان الدمشقي وأبو شمر ويونس بن عمران والفضل الرقاشي ( و ) هؤلاء كلهم ( اتفقوا على أنه تعالى لو عفا ) في القيامة ( عن عاص لعفا عن كل من هو مثله وكذا لو أخرج واحداً من (النار لأخرج كل من هو مثله ( ولم يجزموا بخروج المؤمنين من النار، واختص ابن غيلان أو ( غيلان ) من بينهم (بالقدر)، إذ قد جمع بين الإرجاء والقول بالقدر أي إسناد الأفعال إلى العباد ( والخروج) من حيث أنه قال : يجوز أن لا يكون الإمام قرشيا
The Thawbaniyya: The followers of Thawban al-Murji'i. They said: Faith is knowledge and acknowledgment of God and His messengers and of everything that is not rationally impossible for Him to do. As for what is rationally possible for Him to do, belief in it is not part of faith. They postponed all actions from faith. They were agreed upon by Marwan ibn Ghilan, and it is said Abu Marwan Ghilan al-Dimashqi, and Abu Shamr, and Yunus ibn 'Imran, and al-Fadl al-Raqqashi. And all of them agreed that if He, exalted, were to forgive a sinner in the Hereafter, He would forgive everyone like him, and similarly if He were to remove one from the Fire, He would remove everyone like him. They did not definitively affirm the exit of believers from the Fire. And Ibn Ghilan, or Ghilan, was distinguished among them by [belief in] Qadr, as he combined irja' with Qadr, i.e., attributing actions to servants, and by [the opinion] that the imam need not be from Quraysh.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage describes the Thawbaniyya subsect. They define faith as knowledge and acknowledgment of God, His messengers, and matters that are rationally impossible for God to do (like lying). Matters that are rationally possible are not part of faith. They completely postpone actions from faith. The passage lists several followers, including Marwan ibn Ghilan and others. These followers all agreed on a particular view of God's forgiveness: if God were to forgive a sinner, He would forgive all similar sinners, and similarly if He removes one from the Fire, He removes all like him. They did not affirm definitively that any believers would exit the Fire. Ibn Ghilan is singled out for his belief in Qadr (human free will) and the opinion that the imam does not necessarily have to be from Quraysh, combining irja' with Qadar.

Key Terms
العفو
النار
اتفقوا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Thawbaniyya held that all believers are definitely forgiven and will exit the Fire.
Correction: They only spoke conditionally and did not affirm it as a definite event.

Checkpoint
What did the Thawbaniyya believe about the exit of believers from the Fire?
A) All believers will exit.
B) No believers will exit.
C) They did not definitively affirm it.
D) Only sinful believers will exit.

Key Takeaway
The Thawbaniyya held a conditional uniform view of forgiveness but refrained from asserting that any believers will actually leave Hell.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God were to forgive one sinner only because He is merciful, why would He not forgive every sinner? Do you rely on God's mercy selectively, assuming your sins are less serious than others'? How does the Thawbaniyya's logic force you to examine your own hope for forgiveness?
?
The Thawbaniyya refused to definitively affirm that any believer would exit the Fire. Are you certain of your own salvation? Have you ever truly confronted the possibility that God's justice might require equal treatment for your sins? What would that mean for how you live today?
?
You often assume that because you believe, God will forgive you. But the Thawbaniyya's principle says that if He forgives one, He must forgive all of the same type. Are you willing to have your sins compared to others'? Or do you secretly hope God will overlook what He requires of others? Repentance demands that you stop making exceptions for yourself.

Ibn Ghilan: Qadr and Imamate
Ibn Ghilan's distinct beliefs in Qadr and imamate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Ghilan's distinctive beliefs in Qadr (human free will) and the permissibility of non-Qurayshi imams, which set him apart within the Thawbaniyya.

Core Idea
Ibn Ghilan combined irja' with Qadr and rejected Quraysh requirement for imamate.

Among the Thawbaniyya, Ibn Ghilan stood out for two additional beliefs: affirming human free will (Qadr) and allowing non-Qurayshi imams. These positions made him distinct within the subsect and connected him to broader theological debates.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about Ibn Ghilan
Read the Arabic passage that says Ibn Ghilan (or Ghilan) was distinguished among them by Qadr and by the view that the imam need not be from Quraysh.
Note the parentheses indicate variation in name.
2
Understand his Qadr belief
Qadr here refers to the belief that humans create their own actions (attributing actions to servants). This is a Qadari view, often opposed to predestinarianism.
He combined this with irja' (postponement of works from faith), which was unusual.
3
Understand his imamate view
He held that the imam (caliph) does not have to be from the Quraysh tribe, contradicting the Sunni consensus.
This was a minority position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثوبانية : أصحاب ثوبان المرجئي. قالوا : الإيمان هو المعرفة والإقرار بالله وبرسله وبكل ما لا يجوز في العقل أن يفعله، وأما ما جاز في العقل أن يفعله فليس الاعتقاد به من الإيمان وأخروا العمل كله عن الإيمان ووافقهم على ذلك مروان بن غيلان وقيل : أبو مروان غيلان الدمشقي وأبو شمر ويونس بن عمران والفضل الرقاشي ( و ) هؤلاء كلهم ( اتفقوا على أنه تعالى لو عفا ) في القيامة ( عن عاص لعفا عن كل من هو مثله وكذا لو أخرج واحداً من (النار لأخرج كل من هو مثله ( ولم يجزموا بخروج المؤمنين من النار، واختص ابن غيلان أو ( غيلان ) من بينهم (بالقدر)، إذ قد جمع بين الإرجاء والقول بالقدر أي إسناد الأفعال إلى العباد ( والخروج) من حيث أنه قال : يجوز أن لا يكون الإمام قرشيا
The Thawbaniyya: The followers of Thawban al-Murji'i. They said: Faith is knowledge and acknowledgment of God and His messengers and of everything that is not rationally impossible for Him to do. As for what is rationally possible for Him to do, belief in it is not part of faith. They postponed all actions from faith. They were agreed upon by Marwan ibn Ghilan, and it is said Abu Marwan Ghilan al-Dimashqi, and Abu Shamr, and Yunus ibn 'Imran, and al-Fadl al-Raqqashi. And all of them agreed that if He, exalted, were to forgive a sinner in the Hereafter, He would forgive everyone like him, and similarly if He were to remove one from the Fire, He would remove everyone like him. They did not definitively affirm the exit of believers from the Fire. And Ibn Ghilan, or Ghilan, was distinguished among them by [belief in] Qadr, as he combined irja' with Qadr, i.e., attributing actions to servants, and by [the opinion] that the imam need not be from Quraysh.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage describes the Thawbaniyya subsect. They define faith as knowledge and acknowledgment of God, His messengers, and matters that are rationally impossible for God to do (like lying). Matters that are rationally possible are not part of faith. They completely postpone actions from faith. The passage lists several followers, including Marwan ibn Ghilan and others. These followers all agreed on a particular view of God's forgiveness: if God were to forgive a sinner, He would forgive all similar sinners, and similarly if He removes one from the Fire, He removes all like him. They did not affirm definitively that any believers would exit the Fire. Ibn Ghilan is singled out for his belief in Qadr (human free will) and the opinion that the imam does not necessarily have to be from Quraysh, combining irja' with Qadar.

الإمامة
الإرجاء
الخروج

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think all Thawbaniyya held Qadari views on free will.
Correction: Only Ibn Ghilan among them is reported to have held Qadr; others did not necessarily share this.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a distinctive belief of Ibn Ghilan?
A) Faith includes actions
B) All believers will exit the Fire
C) The imam can be non-Qurayshi
D) God's forgiveness is unconditional

Key Takeaway
Ibn Ghilan uniquely combined Murji'i irja' with Qadari free will and rejected the Qurayshi condition for imamate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Ghilan combined irja' (postponing works) with Qadr (free will) even though these seem contradictory. Are you harboring any incompatible beliefs in your own faith just because they feel comfortable? What would it cost you to align them with the truth?
?
He rejected the requirement that the imam be from Quraysh, breaking from consensus. When you evaluate leaders—whether in your community or your life—what criteria do you use? Are you truly following the teachings of the Salaf, or your own preferences?
?
This passage shows how one man's innovation can set him apart from the mainstream. Have you ever quietly adopted a belief or practice that you know contradicts the way of the early Muslims? If so, what will you do about it starting today?

The Thumuniyya: Definition of Faith and Rulings on Disbelief
Describes the Thumuniyya's definition of faith and rulings on disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Thumuniyya's definition of faith as a set of five components and their criteria for what constitutes disbelief, including specific rulings on leaving prayer, killing a prophet, and prostration to an idol.

Core Idea
Faith has multiple components; abandoning any is disbelief, but some acts are only signs of disbelief.

The Thumuniyya subsect of the Murji'ah held a nuanced view of faith and disbelief. They defined faith as comprising knowledge, affirmation, love, sincerity, and acknowledgment, and they carefully distinguished between actions that are inherently disbelief and those that merely indicate it. This passage presents their key positions and concludes with the identification of the pure Murji'ah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic text and its English translation to get an overview of the Thumuniyya's beliefs.
Notice the list of five components of faith.
2
Analyze the definition of faith
Identify the five components of faith according to the Thumuniyya: knowledge, affirmation, love, sincerity, and acknowledgment. Understand that abandoning any part is considered disbelief.
Contrast this with other Murji'ah definitions that focus only on tasdiq.
3
Examine the specific cases
Look at how the Thumuniyya rule on specific actions: leaving prayer, killing a prophet, and prostration to an idol. Note the reasoning behind each ruling.
Killing a prophet is disbelief because it indicates belying, not because of the act itself.
4
Identify the pure Murji'ah and those combining with Qadr
The passage concludes by naming the pure Murji'ah and listing those who combined irja' with Qadr. Understand the significance of this classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثومنية : أصحاب أبي معاذ الثومني قالوا : الإيمان هو المعرفة والتصديق والمحبة والإخلاص والإقرار بما جاء به الرسول ) وترك كله أو بعضه كفر وليس بعضه إيماناً ولا بعضه أي ولا بعض إيمان، وكل معصية لم يجمع على أنه كفر، فصاحبه يقول إنه فسق وعصى ولا يقال : إنه فاسق ومن ترك الصلاة مستحلا (كفر لتكذيبه بما جاء به النبي (و) من تركها ( بنية القضاء لم يكفر، ومن قتل نبياً أو لطمه ،كفر ، لا لأجل القتل أو اللطمة بل ( لأنه دليل لتكذيبه وبغضه، وبه قال ابن الراوندي وبشر المريسي وقالا : السجود للصنم) ليس كفراً بل هو ( علامة الكفر. فهذه هي المرجئة الخالصة ومنهم من جمع إليه ) ، إي إلى الإرجاء القدر كالصالحي وأبي شمر ومحمد بن شبيب وغيلان
The Thumuniyya: The followers of Abu Mu'adh al-Thumuni. They said: Faith is knowledge, affirmation, love, sincerity, and acknowledgment of what the Messenger brought. Abandoning all or some of it is disbelief. Some of it is not faith, nor is some of it [i.e., not some faith]. Every sin that is not unanimously considered disbelief, its doer is said to have committed sin and disobedience, but not pronounced sinful. Whoever leaves prayer considering it permissible disbelieves due to belying what the Prophet brought. Whoever leaves it with the intention of making it up does not disbelieve. Whoever kills a prophet or slaps him disbelieves, not because of the killing or slapping itself, but because it is evidence of his belying and hatred. This is also the view of Ibn al-Rawandi and Bishr al-Marisi, and they said: Prostration to an idol is not disbelief but a sign of disbelief. These are the pure Murji'ah. Among them are those who combined irja' with Qadr, like al-Salihi, Abu Shamr, Muhammad ibn Shabib, and Ghilan.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage describes the Thumuniyya subsect. They define faith as five components: knowledge, affirmation (tasdiq), love, sincerity (ikhlas), and acknowledgment of what the Prophet brought. Abandoning any part is disbelief. They distinguish between sins that are unanimously considered disbelief and those that are not; for the latter, the doer is sinful but not called a fasiq (sinner) in a definitive sense? Actually they say 'he has committed sin and disobedience, and it is not said he is a fasiq'. They discuss specific cases: leaving prayer while considering it permissible is disbelief; leaving it with intent to make it up is not. Killing or slapping a prophet is disbelief because it indicates belying. They cite Ibn al-Rawandi and Bishr al-Marisi, who said prostration to an idol is not disbelief but a sign of it. The passage concludes that these are the pure Murji'ah, and then mentions those who combined irja' with Qadr, listing several names.

Key Terms
الثومنية
التصديق
الإخلاص
الصلاة
قتل نبي
السجود للصنم
المرجئة الخالصة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Thumuniyya considered any major sin as disbelief.
Correction: They distinguished based on intention: killing a prophet is disbelief because it indicates belying, not because killing itself is a major sin.

Checkpoint
According to the Thumuniyya, why is killing a prophet considered disbelief?
A) Because killing is a major sin.
B) Because it implies belying and hatred of the prophet.
C) Because it violates a consensus.
D) Because it is an act of aggression.

Key Takeaway
The Thumuniyya defined faith as a composite of five elements and judged disbelief based on underlying indications, not merely on external acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly possess all five components of faith as defined by the Thumuniyya? If you examine your heart, is there any lack of love or sincerity that could call your faith into question? What will you do today to strengthen that missing component?
?
Have you ever judged someone's faith based solely on an external action—like missing prayer or committing a sin—without knowing their intention? Will you now commit to leaving judgment of others' iman to Allah, as the Thumuniyya taught?
?
The Thumuniyya say that abandoning prayer with the intention of making it up is not disbelief, but abandoning it while considering it permissible is. How do you view your own prayers? Do you ever delay them with the thought that you'll 'make them up later'—and does that reflect true love and sincerity, or is it a dangerous leniency you need to repent from?

The Najjariyya Sect: Doctrinal Overview
Introduction of the Najjariyya sect and its core doctrines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core doctrines of the Najjariyya sect, including their agreements with both Ash'aris and Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
The Najjariyya blended Ash'ari views on actions with Mu'tazili views on attributes.

Before exploring the subsects of the Najjariyya, we need to grasp the foundational positions of the main sect. This passage introduces their stances on divine actions, human capacity, and attribute theology, showing how they straddle two major theological traditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sect and its founder
Read the opening line to learn the name of the sect and its founder. Note that they are considered among the major Islamic sects.
2
List their agreements with Ash'aris
Identify three doctrines on which the Najjariyya agree with the Ash'aris: creation of actions, ability with the act, and acquisition (kasb). Notice the terminology.
These concern human agency and divine power.
3
List their agreements with Mu'tazila
Find the three points of agreement with the Mu'tazila: negation of eternal attributes (only existential), createdness of speech, and denial of vision of God with eyes.
These are key theological differences from the Ash'aris.
4
Note the additional supporters
See that Dirar ibn 'Amr and Hafs al-Fard also agreed with these positions. This shows the broader context of the sect's views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرقة الخامسة : ) من كبار الفرق الإسلامية ( النجارية أصحاب محمد بن الحسين النجار هم موافقون لأهل في خلق الأفعال وأن الاستطاعة مع الفعل و) أن (العبد يكتسب فعله و) موافقون للمعتزلة في نفي الصفات الوجودية ( وحدوث الكلام ونفي الرؤية بالأبصار ووافقهم على ذلك ضرار بن عمرو وحفص ..الفرد وفرقهم ثلاث : ( الأولى : البرغوثية قالوا كلام الله إذا قرئ عرض وإذا كتب ) بأي شيء كان فهو جسم. ( الثانية : الزعفرانية قالوا كلام الله غيره وكل ما هو غيره مخلوق ومن قال كلام الله : غیر مخلوق فهو كافر الثالثة :المستدركية: استدركوا عليهم ) أي على الزعفرانية ( وقالوا : إنه ) أي كلام الله ( مخلوق مطلقاً لكنا وافقنا السنة الورادة بأن كلام الله غير مخلوق (والإجماع المنعقد عليه ( في نفيه وأولناه بما هذه الصورة ) حكايته ) أي حملنا قولهم : غير مخلوق على أنه غير مخلوق على هذا الترتيب والنظم من هذه الحروف والأصوات بل هو مخلوق على غير هذه الحروف وهذه حكاية عنها، وقالوا : أقوال مخالفينا كلها كذب حتى قولهم : لا إله إلا الله) فإنه كذب أيضاً .
The Fifth Group among the Major Islamic Sects: the Najjariyya, followers of Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Najjar. They agree with the Ash'aris on the creation of actions, that ability is with the act, and that the servant acquires his act. They agree with the Mu'tazila in negating existential attributes, the createdness of speech, and the negation of vision [of God] with eyes. They were agreed upon by Dirar ibn 'Amr and Hafs al-Fard. Their sects are three: First: al-Burghuthiyya. They said: The speech of God, when read, is an accident; when written, it is a body. Second: al-Za'faraniyya. They said: The speech of God is other than Him, and everything other than Him is created. Whoever says the speech of God is uncreated is a disbeliever. Third: al-Mustadrikiyya: They made an objection to the Za'faraniyya and said: It [God's speech] is absolutely created, but we agree with the transmitted Sunnah that God's speech is uncreated, and the consensus held on that in negating it, and we interpret it to mean that it is uncreated in this arrangement and order of letters and sounds, but it is created in other than these letters, and this is an account from them. And they said: The statements of our opponents are all false, even their statement 'There is no god but Allah' is also false.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage describes the Najjariyya sect. They are followers of Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Najjar. They agree with the Ash'aris on the creation of actions, that ability is simultaneous with the act, and that the servant acquires his act (kasb). They agree with the Mu'tazila on three points: denial of eternal attributes (only existential attributes), that speech is created, and that God is not seen with eyes. The sect is divided into three subsects: 1) al-Burghuthiyya: they hold that God's speech, when recited, is an accident, and when written, it is a body. 2) al-Za'faraniyya: they say God's speech is other than Him, and everything other than God is created; they declare someone who says God's speech is uncreated as a disbeliever. 3) al-Mustadrikiyya: they object to the Za'faraniyya and say that God's speech is absolutely created, but they accept the Sunni position that it is uncreated in terms of its arrangement and letters, but actually created in other forms. They also claim that all statements of their opponents are false, even the statement 'There is no god but Allah' interpreted in a different sense.

Key Terms
النجارية
خلق الأفعال
الاستطاعة
الكسب
الصفات الوجودية
حدوث الكلام
نفي الرؤية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following do the Najjariyya share with the Ash'aris according to the passage?
A) Negation of vision of God
B) Creation of actions
C) Createdness of speech
D) Negation of existential attributes

Key Takeaway
The Najjariyya sect combines Ash'ari views on human agency with Mu'tazili views on divine attributes and speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God creates all actions, including your good deeds and your sins, how does that change the way you view your own failures and successes? Do you truly accept responsibility for your actions, or do you sometimes blame God for your choices? What would it mean for you to live out the Najjariyya's view of 'acquisition' (kasb) daily?
?
The Najjariyya denied that God can be seen with physical eyes in the afterlife. How does your belief about seeing God affect your longing for the Hereafter? Do you yearn to see your Lord, or have you become comfortable with a distant, unseen God? This lesson challenges you to examine what you truly hope for in Paradise.
?
These sects based their positions on rational arguments, often prioritizing reason over literal revelation. Are there areas in your faith where you trust your intellect more than the clear texts of the Qur'an and Sunna? Ask yourself: is my belief in God's attributes shaped primarily by what He has revealed about Himself or by what seems logical to me?

The Three Subsects of the Najjariyya
Enumeration of the three Najjariyya subsects and their views on divine speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinct positions of the three Najjariyya subsects—Burghuthiyya, Za'faraniyya, and Mustadrikiyya—on the nature of God's speech.

Core Idea
Three Najjariyya subsects debated whether God's speech is an accident, a body, or absolutely created.

The Najjariyya were not a monolithic group; they split into three subsects with divergent views on the nature of divine speech. This passage details each subsect's unique position, including the controversial claim of the Mustadrikiyya that even the shahada is false according to their opponents.

Guided Path
1
Learn the names of the three subsects
Read the passage to identify the three subsects: al-Burghuthiyya, al-Za'faraniyya, and al-Mustadrikiyya. Note the order.
The third subsect is named for 'making an objection' (istidrak).
2
Understand the Burghuthiyya view
See that the Burghuthiyya distinguish between recited speech (an accident) and written speech (a body). Grasp the materialist implication.
3
Understand the Za'faraniyya view
Note that they define God's speech as other than Him, thus created. They label anyone who says it is uncreated as a disbeliever.
This is a harsh takfiri position.
4
Analyze the Mustadrikiyya view
They object to the Za'faraniyya: while speech is absolutely created, they reinterpret the Sunni statement 'uncreated' to refer to the specific arrangement of letters, not the essence.
This is a hermeneutical compromise.
5
Reflect on the radical claim
The Mustadrikiyya also assert that all statements of opponents are false, including the shahada, when meant in the opponents' sense. This shows their extreme exclusivism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرقة الخامسة : ) من كبار الفرق الإسلامية ( النجارية أصحاب محمد بن الحسين النجار هم موافقون لأهل في خلق الأفعال وأن الاستطاعة مع الفعل و) أن (العبد يكتسب فعله و) موافقون للمعتزلة في نفي الصفات الوجودية ( وحدوث الكلام ونفي الرؤية بالأبصار ووافقهم على ذلك ضرار بن عمرو وحفص ..الفرد وفرقهم ثلاث : ( الأولى : البرغوثية قالوا كلام الله إذا قرئ عرض وإذا كتب ) بأي شيء كان فهو جسم. ( الثانية : الزعفرانية قالوا كلام الله غيره وكل ما هو غيره مخلوق ومن قال كلام الله : غیر مخلوق فهو كافر الثالثة :المستدركية: استدركوا عليهم ) أي على الزعفرانية ( وقالوا : إنه ) أي كلام الله ( مخلوق مطلقاً لكنا وافقنا السنة الورادة بأن كلام الله غير مخلوق (والإجماع المنعقد عليه ( في نفيه وأولناه بما هذه الصورة ) حكايته ) أي حملنا قولهم : غير مخلوق على أنه غير مخلوق على هذا الترتيب والنظم من هذه الحروف والأصوات بل هو مخلوق على غير هذه الحروف وهذه حكاية عنها، وقالوا : أقوال مخالفينا كلها كذب حتى قولهم : لا إله إلا الله) فإنه كذب أيضاً .
The Fifth Group among the Major Islamic Sects: the Najjariyya, followers of Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Najjar. They agree with the Ash'aris on the creation of actions, that ability is with the act, and that the servant acquires his act. They agree with the Mu'tazila in negating existential attributes, the createdness of speech, and the negation of vision [of God] with eyes. They were agreed upon by Dirar ibn 'Amr and Hafs al-Fard. Their sects are three: First: al-Burghuthiyya. They said: The speech of God, when read, is an accident; when written, it is a body. Second: al-Za'faraniyya. They said: The speech of God is other than Him, and everything other than Him is created. Whoever says the speech of God is uncreated is a disbeliever. Third: al-Mustadrikiyya: They made an objection to the Za'faraniyya and said: It [God's speech] is absolutely created, but we agree with the transmitted Sunnah that God's speech is uncreated, and the consensus held on that in negating it, and we interpret it to mean that it is uncreated in this arrangement and order of letters and sounds, but it is created in other than these letters, and this is an account from them. And they said: The statements of our opponents are all false, even their statement 'There is no god but Allah' is also false.

Commentary
This passage describes the Najjariyya sect. They are followers of Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Najjar. They agree with the Ash'aris on the creation of actions, that ability is simultaneous with the act, and that the servant acquires his act (kasb). They agree with the Mu'tazila on three points: denial of eternal attributes (only existential attributes), that speech is created, and that God is not seen with eyes. The sect is divided into three subsects: 1) al-Burghuthiyya: they hold that God's speech, when recited, is an accident, and when written, it is a body. 2) al-Za'faraniyya: they say God's speech is other than Him, and everything other than God is created; they declare someone who says God's speech is uncreated as a disbeliever. 3) al-Mustadrikiyya: they object to the Za'faraniyya and say that God's speech is absolutely created, but they accept the Sunni position that it is uncreated in terms of its arrangement and letters, but actually created in other forms. They also claim that all statements of their opponents are false, even the statement 'There is no god but Allah' interpreted in a different sense.

Key Terms
البرغوثية
الزعفرانية
المستدركية
كلام الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mustadrikiyya fully agree with the Sunni position that the Qur'an is uncreated.
Correction: The Mustadrikiyya only accept the phrase 'uncreated' as a reference to the specific arrangement of letters, not the essence, and they maintain that the speech itself is created.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which subsect holds that the speech of God is a body when written?
A) al-Burghuthiyya
B) al-Za'faraniyya
C) al-Mustadrikiyya
D) All of them

Key Takeaway
The three Najjariyya subsects represent increasingly radical positions on the nature of God's speech, from physical dualism to absolute createdness and takfir.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an—the very words you utter—do you truly believe you are speaking God's eternal speech, or has it become mere routine? If the Burghuthiyya reduces it to an accident when read, what does that do to your reverence for every letter you pronounce?
?
The Mustadrikiyya claimed to affirm the Sunnah but reinterpreted it so radically that even the shahada—your own declaration of faith—could be deemed false by their standard. Is there any area of your own belief where you are reinterpreting clear texts just to fit a comfortable position, rather than submitting fully?
?
The Za'faraniyya excommunicated anyone who said God's speech is uncreated. Are you quick to judge and label others as deviant, perhaps over secondary matters? What would it take for you to extend mercy to those who disagree with you on such issues, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did?

The Jabriyya: Moderate and Pure Determinists
Definition of Jabriyya and its two subtypes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key beliefs of the Jabriyya and the distinction between moderate and pure fatalism.

Core Idea
Jabriyya attributes all actions to Allah, but moderates allow a roleless 'acquisition'.

This passage from al-Mawaqif introduces the Jabriyya sect, one of the major theological groups. It defines the term 'jabr' and then clarifies that not all Jabriyya are extreme — some affirm a concept of kasb without effect. We'll see how they differ from the pure fatalists like the Jahmiyya.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the main points.
Notice the parentheses; they are part of the original text.
2
Understand the definition of jabr
The term 'jabr' is defined as attributing the servant's action to God. This is the core idea of the sect.
3
Identify the two categories
The passage divides Jabriyya into moderate and pure. Note what each affirms about the servant's role.
Moderates affirm kasb without effect; pure deny any power at all.
4
Reflect on the 'tool' analogy
The pure Jabriyya compare the servant to a tool, indicating complete lack of agency. Consider the theological implications.
This extreme view contrasts with the moderate stance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرقة السادسة : ( من تلك الفرق الكبار ( الجبرية : والجبر إسناد فعل العبد إلى الله والجبرية (متوسطة أي غير خالصة في القول بالجبر المحض بل متوسطة بين الجبر والتفويض تثبت للعبد كسبا في الفعل بلا تأثير فيه ( كالأشعرية ) والنجارية والضرارية وخالصة لا تثبته كالجهمية : وهم أصحاب جهم ابن صفوان ( الترمذي ( قالوا : لا قدرة للعبد أصلاً لا مؤثرة ولا كاسبة بل هو بمنزلة السنة
The Sixth Group among those Major Sects: the Jabriyya. Al-Jabr means attributing the servant's action to God. The Jabriyya are of two types: the moderate, which is not purely deterministic but intermediate between jabr and tafwid, and affirms a kasb (acquisition) for the servant in the action without any effect, like the Ash'aris, the Najjariyya, and the Dirariyya; and the pure, which does not affirm it, like the Jahmiyya. They are the followers of Jahm ibn Safwan al-Tirmidhi. They said: The servant has no power at all, neither effective nor acquisitive; rather he is like a tool.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage defines the Jabriyya sect. It first explains 'jabr' as attributing the servant's action to God. It then divides the Jabriyya into two types: moderate and pure. The moderate Jabriyya are not fully deterministic but intermediate between jabr (compulsion) and tafwid (delegation). They affirm for the servant a kasb (acquisition) in the action without any real effect, citing the Ash'aris, Najjariyya, and Dirariyya as examples. The pure Jabriyya do not affirm any kasb at all, and these are the Jahmiyya, followers of Jahm ibn Safwan. They held that the servant has absolutely no power, neither effective nor acquisitive, but is like a tool (the word 'السنة' likely means 'awl' or 'tool', indicating complete lack of agency).

Key Terms
الجبرية
الجبر
التفويض
الكسب
الجهمية
القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Jabriyya deny any human role in actions.
Correction: Moderate Jabriyya affirm a kasb (acquisition) for the servant, though without any effect.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the moderate Jabriyya affirm for the servant?
A) Full free will.
B) A kasb without effect.
C) No capacity at all.
D) A share in creation.

Key Takeaway
The Jabriyya include moderates who affirm a non-effective kasb and pure fatalists who deny any human power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly feel responsible, or do you sometimes rationalize that it was 'all written'? How does the pure Jabriyya's view of the servant as a tool challenge your own sense of accountability before Allah?
?
The moderate Jabriyya affirm a 'kasb' without effect. Is your repentance a mere acquisition with no real turning of the heart? What would it mean to truly own your actions while acknowledging Allah's power?
?
Jahm ibn Safwan said the servant is like a tool. Do you live as though you are a tool in Allah's hands, passively expecting Him to move you, or do you actively strive, knowing that your effort is real even if Allah creates the result?
