The Murji'ah Agreement on Forgiveness and the Role of Qadr
The Murji'ah's agreement on forgiveness and Ibn Ghilan's qadr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core belief shared by all Murji'ah regarding God's forgiveness on the Day of Resurrection and how Ibn Ghilan distinguished himself by combining irja' with qadr.

Core Idea
All Murji'ah agreed that God's forgiveness is uniform, but some also believed in free will.

The Murji'ah are often misunderstood as a monolithic group. This passage reveals their core agreement on divine forgiveness and highlights a key divergence: the inclusion of qadr (free will) by figures like Ibn Ghilan. Let's examine the text to see how these ideas are presented.

Guided Path
1
Read the first part of the passage
Read the Arabic text from the beginning up to the mention of Ibn Ghilan. Focus on the agreement about forgiveness and the lack of certainty about believers leaving Hell.
2
Identify the shared belief
Note the conditional statement: if God forgives one, He forgives all similar. This shows the Murji'ah view on God's justice.
3
Examine Ibn Ghilan's position
Ibn Ghilan is singled out for combining irja' with qadr. Also note his view that the imam need not be Qurayshi.
This marks a sub-group within the Murji'ah.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this belief in uniform forgiveness affects the understanding of faith and deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واتفقوا على أنه تعالى لو عفا في القيامة عن عاص لعفا عن كل من هو مثله وكذا لو أخرج واحداً من النار لأخرج كل من هو مثله ولم يجزموا بخروج المؤمنين من النار، واختص ابن غيلان أو غيلان من بينهم بالقدر، إذ قد جمع بين الإرجاء والقول بالقدر أي إسناد الأفعال إلى العباد والخروج من حيث أنه قال: يجوز أن لا يكون الإمام قرشيا. الثومنية: أصحاب أبي معاذ الثومني قالوا: الإيمان هو المعرفة والتصديق والمحبة والإخلاص والإقرار بما جاء به الرسول وترك كله أو بعضه كفر وليس بعضه إيماناً ولا بعضه أي ولا بعض إيمان، وكل معصية لم يجمع على أنه كفر، فصاحبه يقول إنه فسق وعصى ولا يقال: إنه فاسق ومن ترك الصلاة مستحلا كفر لتكذيبه بما جاء به النبي ومن تركها بنية القضاء لم يكفر، ومن قتل نبياً أو لطمه كفر، لا لأجل القتل أو اللطمة بل لأنه دليل لتكذيبه وبغضه، وبه قال ابن الراوندي وبشر المريسي وقالا: السجود للصنم ليس كفراً بل هو علامة الكفر. فهذه هي المرجئة الخالصة ومنهم من جمع إليه أي إلى الإرجاء القدر كالصالحي وأبي شمر ومحمد بن شبيب وغيلان.
And they all agreed that He, exalted, if He forgives a disobedient one on the Day of Resurrection, He would forgive everyone like him, and likewise if He brings out one from the Fire, He would bring out everyone like him, and they did not assert decisively the exit of the believers from the Fire. And Ibn Ghilan or Ghilan was distinguished among them by qadr, for he combined irja' with the saying of qadr, i.e., attributing actions to servants, and exit in that he said: It is permissible that the imam not be Qurayshi. Ath-Thumuniyyah: the followers of Abu Mu'adh ath-Thumuni said: Faith is knowledge, affirmation, love, sincerity, and acknowledgment of what the Messenger brought; abandoning all or part of it is unbelief, and neither part of it is faith, nor any part of it, i.e., no part of faith. And every sin that is not unanimously agreed to be unbelief, its doer says it is transgression and disobedience, and it is not said: he is a transgressor. And whoever abandons prayer considering it lawful becomes an unbeliever because of his denial of what the Prophet brought, and whoever abandons it with the intention of making it up does not become an unbeliever. And whoever kills a prophet or slaps him becomes an unbeliever, not because of the killing or the slap, but because it is evidence of his denial and hatred. And Ibn ar-Rawandi and Bishr al-Marisi said likewise, and they said: Prostration to an idol is not unbelief but is a sign of unbelief. So these are the pure Murji'ah, and among them are those who combined with it, i.e., to irja', qadr, such as as-Salihi, Abu Shamar, Muhammad ibn Shabib, and Ghilan.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage classifies the Murji'ah sect and its various sub-groups. It begins by stating the common agreement among all Murji'ah that if God forgives one disobedient person in the afterlife, He will forgive all similar persons; likewise, if He removes one from Hell, He will remove all similar. However, they did not definitively assert that believers will exit the Fire. Then it singles out Ibn Ghilan (or Ghilan) as one who combined irja' with qadr, meaning he attributed actions to servants and held that the imam need not be Qurayshi. The passage then introduces the Thumuniyyah sub-group, followers of Abu Mu'adh ath-Thumuni, who defined faith as a combination of knowledge, affirmation, love, sincerity, and acknowledgment of the Prophet's message. According to them, abandoning any part of this is unbelief, and each component is not faith by itself. They distinguished between sins that are unanimously agreed to be unbelief and those that are not; the latter are merely transgression, not sufficient to label one a 'fasiq.' They ruled that abandoning prayer intentionally while deeming it lawful is unbelief due to denial, but abandoning it with the intention of making it up is not. Killing or slapping a prophet is unbelief not because of the act itself but because it indicates denial and hatred. Ibn ar-Rawandi and Bishr al-Marisi agreed and added that prostrating to an idol is not unbelief but a sign of it. The passage concludes by stating that these described groups constitute the 'pure Murji'ah,' and among them are those who also held qadr, such as as-Salihi, Abu Shamar, Muhammad ibn Shabib, and Ghilan.

Key Terms
المرجئة
الإرجاء
القدر
ابن غيلان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all Murji'ah rejected qadr.
Correction: Some Murji'ah, like Ibn Ghilan, combined irja' with qadr, accepting free will.

Checkpoint
What did the Murji'ah agree upon regarding God's forgiveness on the Day of Resurrection?
A) God forgives only those who repent.
B) If God forgives one, He forgives all similar.
C) God forgives no one.
D) God forgives only the prophets.

Key Takeaway
The Murji'ah believed that God's forgiveness is uniform for all similar disobedient believers, and some like Ibn Ghilan also advocated for free will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever assume that because God is merciful, He will automatically forgive you regardless of how you live? How does the Murji'ah's refusal to decisively affirm exit from the Fire challenge that comfortable assumption? What would change in your daily choices if you truly believed your final state is not guaranteed?
?
Ibn Ghilan insisted that actions are attributed to you—you are responsible. Where in your life do you subtly deny that responsibility by blaming circumstances, other people, or even God's decree for your sins? Be concrete: name one specific habit or excuse you need to stop hiding behind.
?
The Murji'ah said that if God forgives one disobedient person, He forgives all like him. Does your heart accept that God's forgiveness is truly uniform—that He does not play favorites? Or do you secretly believe some sins (or sinners) are beyond His mercy? If that belief is in you, what does it say about your understanding of God's justice and your own need for humility?

The Thumuniyyah Sub-Group: Faith, Sin, and Unbelief
The Thumuniyyah's definition of faith and rulings on sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Thumuniyyah definition of faith and their rulings on sins such as abandoning prayer and harming prophets.

Core Idea
For the Thumuniyyah, faith is a composite of multiple acts, and only intentional denial makes an act unbelief.

The Thumuniyyah, a sub-group of the Murji'ah, had a detailed view of faith that included knowledge, affirmation, love, sincerity, and acknowledgment. They distinguished between sins that are unbelief and those that are mere transgression. This passage explains their nuanced rulings on prayer, killing prophets, and even prostration to idols.

Guided Path
1
Read the Thumuniyyah section
Read from 'الثومنية: أصحاب أبي معاذ الثومني...' to the end of the passage. Pay attention to the definition of faith and the examples given.
2
Understand their definition of faith
Faith is a combination of knowledge, affirmation, love, sincerity, and acknowledgment. Abandoning any part is unbelief, but each part alone is not faith.
This is a multi-component view.
3
Examine the rulings on sins
Note the distinction between sins that are unanimously agreed to be unbelief (like denying the Prophet) and those that are not. Abandoning prayer with intention to make up is not unbelief, but killing a prophet is unbelief because it indicates denial.
4
Consider the statement on prostration to idols
Ibn ar-Rawandi and Bishr al-Marisi said prostration to an idol is not unbelief but a sign of it. This shows their emphasis on intention and underlying belief.
5
Conclude with the classification
The passage ends by stating these are the 'pure Murji'ah' and mentions others who also held qadr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واتفقوا على أنه تعالى لو عفا في القيامة عن عاص لعفا عن كل من هو مثله وكذا لو أخرج واحداً من النار لأخرج كل من هو مثله ولم يجزموا بخروج المؤمنين من النار، واختص ابن غيلان أو غيلان من بينهم بالقدر، إذ قد جمع بين الإرجاء والقول بالقدر أي إسناد الأفعال إلى العباد والخروج من حيث أنه قال: يجوز أن لا يكون الإمام قرشيا. الثومنية: أصحاب أبي معاذ الثومني قالوا: الإيمان هو المعرفة والتصديق والمحبة والإخلاص والإقرار بما جاء به الرسول وترك كله أو بعضه كفر وليس بعضه إيماناً ولا بعضه أي ولا بعض إيمان، وكل معصية لم يجمع على أنه كفر، فصاحبه يقول إنه فسق وعصى ولا يقال: إنه فاسق ومن ترك الصلاة مستحلا كفر لتكذيبه بما جاء به النبي ومن تركها بنية القضاء لم يكفر، ومن قتل نبياً أو لطمه كفر، لا لأجل القتل أو اللطمة بل لأنه دليل لتكذيبه وبغضه، وبه قال ابن الراوندي وبشر المريسي وقالا: السجود للصنم ليس كفراً بل هو علامة الكفر. فهذه هي المرجئة الخالصة ومنهم من جمع إليه أي إلى الإرجاء القدر كالصالحي وأبي شمر ومحمد بن شبيب وغيلان.
And they all agreed that He, exalted, if He forgives a disobedient one on the Day of Resurrection, He would forgive everyone like him, and likewise if He brings out one from the Fire, He would bring out everyone like him, and they did not assert decisively the exit of the believers from the Fire. And Ibn Ghilan or Ghilan was distinguished among them by qadr, for he combined irja' with the saying of qadr, i.e., attributing actions to servants, and exit in that he said: It is permissible that the imam not be Qurayshi. And every sin that is not unanimously agreed to be unbelief, its doer says it is transgression and disobedience, and it is not said: he is a transgressor. And whoever abandons prayer considering it lawful becomes an unbeliever because of his denial of what the Prophet brought, and whoever abandons it with the intention of making it up does not become an unbeliever. And whoever kills a prophet or slaps him becomes an unbeliever, not because of the killing or the slap, but because it is evidence of his denial and hatred. And Ibn ar-Rawandi and Bishr al-Marisi said likewise, and they said: Prostration to an idol is not unbelief but is a sign of unbelief. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That prostrating to an idol is always considered unbelief by all Murji'ah.
Correction: Some Murji'ah, like Ibn ar-Rawandi and Bishr al-Marisi, considered prostration to an idol a sign of unbelief, not unbelief itself.

Checkpoint
According to the Thumuniyyah, what is the status of a person who abandons prayer with the intention of making it up later?
A) He becomes an unbeliever.
B) He does not become an unbeliever.
C) He becomes a fasiq.
D) He is considered a Muslim without sin.

Key Takeaway
The Thumuniyyah defined faith as a combination of five elements and ruled that only acts indicating denial or hatred constitute unbelief, while other sins are mere transgression.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever evaluate your own actions by their outward form or by what they reveal about your heart? The Thumuniyyah said prostration to an idol is not unbelief but a sign. What do your daily actions—like prayer, charity, or even small sins—reveal about your inner beliefs? Are you willing to examine your heart's true posture toward Allah and His Messenger, or do you settle for outward compliance? Commit today to ask Allah to purify your intentions and to make your actions true reflections of faith, not just habits.
?
The Thumuniyyah distinguished between abandoning prayer deeming it lawful (unbelief) and abandoning it with intention to make up (not unbelief). How often do you postpone your prayers thinking you can make them up later? Is your postponement born of laziness or genuine necessity? Ask yourself: does my neglect reveal a neglect of the value of prayer in my heart? What would it take for you to treat every prayer as non-negotiable?
?
Consider the statement: 'Whoever kills a prophet becomes an unbeliever, not because of the killing, but because it is evidence of his denial and hatred.' What does this say about the root of unbelief? Do you harbor any hidden resentment toward the teachings of the Prophet (peace be upon him) or any aspect of the Sunnah? Even small resistance? This lesson warns that outward acts stem from inner states. Pray that Allah removes any trace of hatred or denial from your heart.

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
4 min
The Najjariyyah Sect and Its First Two Sub-Groups
Describes Najjariyyah's agreements and first two sub-groups

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core beliefs of the Najjariyyah sect and the views of its first two sub-groups on the nature of God's speech.

Core Idea
The Najjariyyah tried to bridge Ash'ari and Mu'tazili views but split over God's speech.

The Najjariyyah, followers of Muhammad ibn al-Husayn an-Najjar, adopted a middle position on several theological issues. However, their followers disagreed sharply on the nature of the Qur'an. This lesson introduces the sect's foundational teachings and the first two splinter groups, al-Barghuthiyyah and az-Za'faraniyyah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Najjariyyah's agreements
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting how the Najjariyyah agreed with the Ash'aris on three points and with the Mu'tazila on three points.
The phrase 'أهل' refers to the Ash'aris in this context.
2
Identify the three areas of agreement with Ash'aris
Find the three specific doctrines: creation of actions, capacity with the act, and acquisition (kasb). Understand what each means briefly.
3
Identify the three areas of agreement with Mu'tazila
Find the three doctrines: negation of existential attributes, temporality of speech (Qur'an created), and negation of beatific vision.
These are core Mu'tazili positions.
4
Learn about al-Barghuthiyyah's view on God's speech
This sub-group held that God's speech is an accident when recited and a body when written. Consider the implications of this materialistic view.
5
Learn about az-Za'faraniyyah's view on God's speech
They held that God's speech is other than God and therefore created, and declared anyone who says it is uncreated as an unbeliever.
This is a more extreme version of the Mu'tazili position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرقة الخامسة: النجارية أصحاب محمد بن الحسين النجار هم موافقون لأهل في خلق الأفعال وأن الاستطاعة مع الفعل و أن العبد يكتسب فعله و موافقون للمعتزلة في نفي الصفات الوجودية وحدوث الكلام ونفي الرؤية بالأبصار ووافقهم على ذلك ضرار بن عمرو وحفص ..الفرد وفرقهم ثلاث: الأولى: البرغوثية قالوا كلام الله إذا قرئ عرض وإذا كتب بأي شيء كان فهو جسم. الثانية: الزعفرانية قالوا كلام الله غيره وكل ما هو غيره مخلوق ومن قال كلام الله غير مخلوق فهو كافر الثالثة: المستدركية: استدركوا عليهم أي على الزعفرانية وقالوا: إنه أي كلام الله مخلوق مطلقاً لكنا وافقنا السنة الورادة بأن كلام الله غير مخلوق والإجماع المنعقد عليه في نفيه وأولناه بما هذه الصورة حكايته أي حملنا قولهم: غير مخلوق على أنه غير مخلوق على هذا الترتيب والنظم من هذه الحروف والأصوات بل هو مخلوق على غير هذه الحروف وهذه حكاية عنها، وقالوا: أقوال مخالفينا كلها كذب حتى قولهم: لا إله إلا الله فإنه كذب أيضاً.
The fifth sect: an-Najjariyyah, followers of Muhammad ibn al-Husayn an-Najjar. They agree with the people [i.e., Ash'aris] on the creation of actions, that capacity is with the act, and that the servant acquires his act, and they agree with the Mu'tazila in negating existential attributes, the temporality of speech, and negating vision with eyes. Dirar ibn 'Amr and Hafs ... al-Fard agreed with them on that. Their sub-groups are three: First: al-Barghuthiyyah, who said that the speech of God, when read, is an accident, and when written in any thing, it is a body. Second: az-Za'faraniyyah, who said that the speech of God is other than Him, and everything other than Him is created; whoever says that the speech of God is uncreated is an unbeliever. Third: al-Mustadrikiyyah, who corrected them, i.e., the Za'faraniyyah, and said: Indeed it, i.e., the speech of God, is absolutely created, but we agree with the transmitted Sunnah that the speech of God is uncreated, and the consensus held on its negation, and we interpret it as this form of its narration, i.e., we carry their statement 'uncreated' to mean that it is uncreated in this order and arrangement of these letters and sounds, but it is created in other than these letters, and this is a narration of it. And they said: All statements of our opponents are false, even their statement 'There is no god but God,' for it is also false.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage defines the Najjariyyah sect, founded by Muhammad ibn al-Husayn an-Najjar, and lists its three sub-groups. It first notes that the Najjariyyah agreed with the Ash'aris (referred to as 'ahl' here) on the creation of actions, that capacity is simultaneous with the act, and that the servant acquires his action (kasb). However, they agreed with the Mu'tazila on negating the eternal attributes (other than essence), the temporality of the Qur'an, and denying the beatific vision. Dirar ibn 'Amr and Hafs al-Fard concurred. The Najjariyyah then split into three sub-groups: 1) al-Barghuthiyyah, who held that God's speech, when recited, is an accident ('arad), and when written, becomes a body. 2) az-Za'faraniyyah, who claimed that God's speech is something other than God, and everything other than God is created; they declared as unbeliever anyone who says God's speech is uncreated. 3) al-Mustadrikiyyah, who corrected the Za'faraniyyah by asserting that God's speech is absolutely created, yet they attempted to reconcile with the Sunni position by interpreting the phrase 'uncreated' to mean that it is uncreated in terms of its order and arrangement when recited, but the letters and sounds themselves are created. They further made the extreme claim that all statements of their opponents are false, even the testimony of faith, 'La ilaha illa Allah,' calling it false.

Key Terms
النجارية
كسب
خلق الأفعال
البرغوثية
الزعفرانية
كلام الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Najjariyyah were identical to the Mu'tazila on all points.
Correction: They agreed with Ash'aris on the creation of actions, capacity with act, and acquisition, and with Mu'tazila on negation of attributes, temporality of speech, and denial of vision.

Checkpoint

A) The creation of actions
B) The negation of beatific vision
C) The acquisition of acts
D) The capacity is before the act

Key Takeaway
The Najjariyyah sought a middle path but their followers split over the nature of God's speech, leading to diverse and conflicting claims.

The Mustadrikiyyah: Reconciliation and Extremism
Describes the Mustadrikiyyah's corrective view on God's speech and their extreme claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the position of the Mustadrikiyyah, who tried to reconcile the createdness of the Qur'an with Sunni orthodoxy by reinterpreting 'uncreated', and their extreme declaration that all statements of opponents are false.

Core Idea
The Mustadrikiyyah reinterpreted 'uncreated' to mean uncreated in arrangement only, and declared even the shahada of opponents false.

The Mustadrikiyyah emerged as a corrective to the Za'faraniyyah, asserting that God's speech is absolutely created while attempting to harmonize with Sunni tradition. Their hermeneutical move allowed them to accept the Sunni phrase 'uncreated' but emptied it of its usual meaning. They then made the radical claim that all statements of their theological opponents, including the testimony of faith, are false.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-Mustadrikiyyah
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, noting that they 'corrected' the Za'faraniyyah.
The term 'استدركوا عليهم' means they corrected or supplemented them.
2
Understand their core claim
They assert that God's speech is absolutely created (مخلوق مطلقاً). This agrees with the Za'faraniyyah on the basic point.
3
Observe their hermeneutical strategy
They accept the Sunni statement that God's speech is uncreated, but interpret 'uncreated' to mean the order and arrangement (النظم والترتيب) of letters and sounds, not the letters and sounds themselves.
This is a subtle redefinition to avoid outright contradiction with the Sunnah.
4
Reflect on their extreme conclusion
They declared that all statements of their opponents are false, including the shahada 'La ilaha illa Allah'. This shows a radical exclusivism.
This goes beyond theological disagreement to a blanket dismissal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرقة الخامسة: النجارية أصحاب محمد بن الحسين النجار هم موافقون لأهل في خلق الأفعال وأن الاستطاعة مع الفعل و أن العبد يكتسب فعله و موافقون للمعتزلة في نفي الصفات الوجودية وحدوث الكلام ونفي الرؤية بالأبصار ووافقهم على ذلك ضرار بن عمرو وحفص ..الفرد وفرقهم ثلاث: الأولى: البرغوثية قالوا كلام الله إذا قرئ عرض وإذا كتب بأي شيء كان فهو جسم. الثانية: الزعفرانية قالوا كلام الله غيره وكل ما هو غيره مخلوق ومن قال كلام الله غير مخلوق فهو كافر الثالثة: المستدركية: استدركوا عليهم أي على الزعفرانية وقالوا: إنه أي كلام الله مخلوق مطلقاً لكنا وافقنا السنة الورادة بأن كلام الله غير مخلوق والإجماع المنعقد عليه في نفيه وأولناه بما هذه الصورة حكايته أي حملنا قولهم: غير مخلوق على أنه غير مخلوق على هذا الترتيب والنظم من هذه الحروف والأصوات بل هو مخلوق على غير هذه الحروف وهذه حكاية عنها، وقالوا: أقوال مخالفينا كلها كذب حتى قولهم: لا إله إلا الله فإنه كذب أيضاً.
The fifth sect: an-Najjariyyah, followers of Muhammad ibn al-Husayn an-Najjar. They agree with the people [i.e., Ash'aris] on the creation of actions, that capacity is with the act, and that the servant acquires his act, and they agree with the Mu'tazila in negating existential attributes, the temporality of speech, and negating vision with eyes. Dirar ibn 'Amr and Hafs ... al-Fard agreed with them on that. Their sub-groups are three: First: al-Barghuthiyyah, who said that the speech of God, when read, is an accident, and when written in any thing, it is a body. Second: az-Za'faraniyyah, who said that the speech of God is other than Him, and everything other than Him is created; whoever says that the speech of God is uncreated is an unbeliever. Third: al-Mustadrikiyyah, who corrected them, i.e., the Za'faraniyyah, and said: Indeed it, i.e., the speech of God, is absolutely created, but we agree with the transmitted Sunnah that the speech of God is uncreated, and the consensus held on its negation, and we interpret it as this form of its narration, i.e., we carry their statement 'uncreated' to mean that it is uncreated in this order and arrangement of these letters and sounds, but it is created in other than these letters, and this is a narration of it. And they said: All statements of our opponents are false, even their statement 'There is no god but God,' for it is also false.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage defines the Najjariyyah sect, founded by Muhammad ibn al-Husayn an-Najjar, and lists its three sub-groups. It first notes that the Najjariyyah agreed with the Ash'aris (referred to as 'ahl' here) on the creation of actions, that capacity is simultaneous with the act, and that the servant acquires his action (kasb). However, they agreed with the Mu'tazila on negating the eternal attributes (other than essence), the temporality of the Qur'an, and denying the beatific vision. Dirar ibn 'Amr and Hafs al-Fard concurred. The Najjariyyah then split into three sub-groups: 1) al-Barghuthiyyah, who held that God's speech, when recited, is an accident ('arad), and when written, becomes a body. 2) az-Za'faraniyyah, who claimed that God's speech is something other than God, and everything other than God is created; they declared as unbeliever anyone who says God's speech is uncreated. 3) al-Mustadrikiyyah, who corrected the Za'faraniyyah by asserting that God's speech is absolutely created, yet they attempted to reconcile with the Sunni position by interpreting the phrase 'uncreated' to mean that it is uncreated in terms of its order and arrangement when recited, but the letters and sounds themselves are created. They further made the extreme claim that all statements of their opponents are false, even the testimony of faith, 'La ilaha illa Allah,' calling it false.

The Jabriyyah: Definition and Two Types
Sanusi defines the Jabriyyah and distinguishes moderate from pure types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of jabr and the two main types of Jabriyyah: moderate (which affirm kasb) and pure (which deny any power in the servant).

Core Idea
The Jabriyyah sect splits into moderate (Ash'ariyya-style) and pure (Jahmiyya) types, differing on the servant's power.

Before exploring the specific doctrines of the Jabriyyah, it is essential to understand their basic stance: they attribute all human actions to God. This lesson introduces the two branches of Jabriyyah—the moderate ones who affirm a non-effective kasb, and the pure ones who deny any power in the servant. This classification sets the stage for understanding their theological controversies.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of jabr
Read the Arabic passage once to get the lexical meaning of jabr: ascribing the servant's act to God. This is the foundational concept.
Notice that the definition is concise.
2
Identify the moderate type
Find the description of moderate Jabriyyah. Note which groups are listed as examples (Ash'ariyya, Najjariyya, Dirariyya) and what they affirm: kasb without effect.
3
Identify the pure type
Find the description of pure Jabriyyah (Jahmiyya). Note that they do not affirm even kasb. Recognize the founder: Jahm ibn Safwan.
This distinction is crucial for understanding later doctrines.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرقة السادسة: الجبرية والجبر إسناد فعل العبد إلى الله والجبرية متوسطة أي غير خالصة في القول بالجبر المحض بل متوسطة بين الجبر والتفويض تثبت للعبد كسبا في الفعل بلا تأثير فيه كالأشعرية والنجارية والضرارية وخالصة لا تثبته كالجهمية: وهم أصحاب جهم ابن صفوان الترمذي قالوا: لا قدرة للعبد أصلاً لا مؤثرة ولا كاسبة بل هو بمنزلة الجمادات فيما يوجد منها والله يعلم الشيء قبل وقوعه وعلمه حادث لا في محل، ولا يتصف الله بما يوصف به غيره إذ يلزم منه التشبيه كالعلم والقدرة، لو أبدل القدرة بالحياة كما ذكره الآمدي لكان أولى لأن جهماً لا يثبت لغير الله قدرته، والجنة والنار تفنيان بعد دخول أهلهما فيهما حتى لا يبقى موجود سوى سبحانه، ووافقوا المعتزلة في نفي الرؤية وخلق الكلام وإيجاب المعرفة بالعقل قبل ورود الشرع.
The sixth sect: al-Jabriyyah. And jabr is the attribution of the servant's action to God. And the Jabriyyah are [of two types]: moderate, i.e., not pure in the claim of absolute jabr, but moderate between jabr and tafwid, affirming for the servant a kasb in the act without effect in it, like the Ash'ariyya, Najjariyya, and Dirariyya; and pure, who do not affirm it, like the Jahmiyya: they are the followers of Jahm ibn Safwan at-Tirmidhi. They said: There is no power for the servant at all, neither effective nor acquisitive; rather he is like inanimate objects in what occurs from them. And God knows the thing before its occurrence, and His knowledge is temporal (hadith) not in a locus. And God is not described by what others are described by, for that would entail tashbih, like knowledge and power; if one substituted power with life as al-Amidi mentioned, it would be more appropriate, because Jahm does not affirm power for other than God. And Paradise and Hell will perish after their inhabitants enter them, until no existent remains except Him, glorified. And they agreed with the Mu'tazila in negating the vision [of God], the creation of speech, and the obligation of knowledge through reason before the advent of revelation.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage defines the Jabriyyah sect (determinists) and divides it into two main types. It first defines jabr as attributing the servant's action entirely to God. The moderate Jabriyyah, such as the Ash'ariyya, Najjariyya, and Dirariyya, affirm a 'kasb' for the servant—an acquisition of the act that does not produce any real effect. In contrast, the pure Jabriyyah, namely the Jahmiyya (followers of Jahm ibn Safwan), deny any power in the servant whatsoever, neither effective nor acquisitive, likening the servant to inanimate objects. The text then outlines key Jahmi doctrines: God's knowledge is temporal (hadith) and not subsisting in a locus; God cannot be described by attributes that apply to creatures (like knowledge and power) because that would imply anthropomorphism (tashbih). The author notes that al-Amidi suggested using 'life' instead of 'power' would be better since Jahm denies power to anyone but God. Additional doctrines include the annihilation of Paradise and Hell after their inhabitants enter them, so that only God remains, and agreement with the Mu'tazila on denying the beatific vision, affirming the creation of the Qur'an, and asserting that knowledge of God is obligatory by reason prior to revelation.

Key Terms
الجبرية
الكسب
الجهمية
جهم بن صفوان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Jabriyyah deny the servant any role in actions.
Correction: Only the pure Jabriyyah (Jahmiyya) deny all power; the moderate ones affirm a non-effective kasb.

Checkpoint
Which of the following groups is considered moderate Jabriyyah?
A) Jahmiyya
B) Ash'ariyya
C) Mu'tazila
D) Qadariyya

Key Takeaway
The Jabriyyah is divided into two types: moderate (who affirm kasb) and pure (who deny all power in the servant).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every action you do is ultimately attributed to Allah, where does your personal accountability lie? How does this truth change the way you view your sins and good deeds?
?
The moderate Jabriyyah affirm a 'kasb'—an acquisition without effect. Do you live as though your choices truly matter, or have you ever used divine decree as an excuse for inaction? Be honest with yourself.
?
The pure Jabriyyah deny any power in the servant. Is there a part of your heart that secretly wishes you had no responsibility? How does this passage confront that desire and call you to take ownership of your faith and actions?

Doctrines of the Jahmiyyah (Pure Jabriyyah)
Sanusi enumerates the distinctive doctrines of the Jahmiyya sect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key doctrines of the Jahmiyya, including their views on human power, God's knowledge, divine attributes, annihilation of Paradise and Hell, and their agreement with the Mu'tazila on certain issues.

Core Idea
The Jahmiyya held radical views: no human power, temporal divine knowledge, denial of anthropomorphism, and annihilation of Paradise and Hell.

The pure Jabriyyah, known as the Jahmiyya, developed several controversial doctrines. This lesson examines their specific teachings as outlined by Sanusi, including their stance on human power, divine attributes, the fate of Paradise and Hell, and their points of agreement with the Mu'tazila. Understanding these doctrines is crucial for recognizing the boundaries of orthodox Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Jahmiyya's view on human power
Find the opening statement: 'There is no power for the servant at all, neither effective nor acquisitive.' Note the comparison to inanimate objects.
2
Note their doctrine on God's knowledge
Identify the claim that God's knowledge is temporal (hadith) and not in a locus. This implies change in God, which is problematic.
3
Understand their rejection of anthropomorphic attributes
Read how they avoid describing God by attributes like knowledge and power to prevent tashbih. Note al-Amidi's suggested substitution with life.
4
Recognize teachings on annihilation and Mu'tazili agreements
Notice the belief that Paradise and Hell will perish after entrance. Then see the three points of agreement with the Mu'tazila: negating vision, creation of speech, rational obligation before revelation.
These points are important for understanding historical theological debates.

The Mushabbihah and Its Shi'a Extremist Branch
Defines Mushabbihah and describes its Shi'a extremists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the Mushabbihah sect and the specific doctrines of its extremist Shi'a sub-group.

Core Idea
Mushabbihah liken Allah to creation, especially the Shi'a extremists.

This passage introduces the seventh sect, the Mushabbihah, who compare Allah to created beings. To understand their diversity, the author first defines the group as a whole and then focuses on one sub-group: the extremist Shi'a, who held extreme corporealist and incarnationist beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of Mushabbihah
Read the opening lines where the author defines the group as those who liken Allah to created things. Note that they are considered one sect despite internal differences in method.
2
Identify the first sub-group
Find the mention of 'Mushabbihah of the extremists of the Shi'a' and the named sects: as-Saba'iyya, al-Bayaniyya, al-Mughiriyya. Notice their beliefs include corporealism, movement, transition, and incarnation.
These doctrines are said to have been presented earlier in the text.
3
Understand the significance
Ask yourself why the author singles out this sub-group first. Reflect on how their views represent an extreme form of anthropomorphism that the author rejects.
The next lessons will cover the other sub-groups.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرقة السابعة: المشبهة شبهوا الله بالمخلوقات ومثلوه بالحادثات وهم لأجل ذلك جعلناهم فرقة واحدة قائلة بالتشبيه وإن اختلفوا في طريقه فمنهم مشبهة غلاة الشيعة كالسبائية والبيانية والمغيرية وغيرهم كما تقدم من مذاهبهم بالتجسيم والحركة والانتقال والحلول في الأجسام إلى غير ذلك، ومنهم مشبهة الحشوية كمضر وكهمس والهيجمي قالوا هو جسم لا كالأجسام من لحم ودم ولا كاللحوم والدماء وله الأعضاء والجوارح ويجوز عليه الملامسة والمصافحة والمعانقة للمخلصين الذين يزورونه في الدنيا ويزورهم حتى نقل أنه قال بعضهم: اعفوني عن اللحية والفرج وسلوني عما وراءه، ومنهم مشبهة الكرامية أصحاب أبي عبد الله محمد بن کرام قيل: هو بكسر الكاف وتخفيف الراء وفيه قيل: متناه الفقه فقه أبي حنيفة وحده والدين دين محمد بن کرام وأقوالهم متعددة مختلفة غير أنها لا تنتهي إلى من يعبأ به ويبالي بقوله فاقتصرنا على ما قاله زعيمهم وهو أن الله على العرش من جهة العلو مماس له من الصفحة العليا ويجوز عليه الحركة والنزول واختلفوا أيملا العرش أم لا يملأه بل هو على بعضه؟، وقال بعضهم: ليس هو على العرش بل هو محاذ للعرش واختلف أببعد متناه أو غيره؟ ومنهم من أطلق عليه لفظ الجسم ثم اختلفوا هل هو في الجهات كلها أو متناه من جهة تحت فقط أو لا؟ أي ليس متناهياً بل هو غير متناه في جميع الجهات وقالوا: تحل الحوادث في ذاته وزعموا أنه إنما يقدر عليها أي على الحوادث الحالة فيه دون الخارجة عن ذاته ويجب على الله أن يكون أول خلقه حياً يصح منه الاستدلال، و سوى المعجزة والعصمة وصاحبها أي صاحب تلك الصفة رسول بسبب اتصافه بها من غير إرسال ويجب على الله إرساله لا غير أي لا يجوز إرسال غير الرسول وهو حينئذ أي حين إذا أرسل مرسل وكل مرسل رسول بلا عكس كلي ويجوز عزله أي عزل المرسل عن كونه مرسلاً دون الرسول، فإنه لا يتصور عزله عن كونه رسولاً.
The seventh sect: al-Mushabbihah. They likened God to created things and compared Him to temporal things, and for that reason we made them one sect that speaks of tashbih, although they differ in their method. Among them are the Mushabbihah of the extremists of the Shi'a, such as as-Saba'iyya, al-Bayaniyya, al-Mughiriyya, and others, as their doctrines have been presented earlier, involving corporealism, movement, transition, incarnation in bodies, and so on. And among them are the Mushabbihah of the Hashwiyya, such as Mudar, Kuhmas, and al-Hayjami. They said: He is a body not like bodies, of flesh and blood, and not like flesh and blood; He has organs and limbs, and touching, shaking hands, and embracing are permissible for Him with the sincere ones who visit Him in this world and whom He visits, until it is reported that one of them said: 'Spare me the beard and the private parts, and ask me about what is beyond them.' And among them are the Mushabbihah of the Karramiyya, followers of Abu 'Abdullah Muhammad ibn Karram. It is said: 'He' is with a kasr of the kaf and tashdid of the ra', and regarding him it is said: 'The jurisprudence is the jurisprudence of Abu Hanifa alone, and the religion is the religion of Muhammad ibn Karram.' Their statements are numerous and various, but they do not lead to one whose saying is regarded or considered, so we confined ourselves to what their leader said: that God is upon the Throne from the direction of height, touching it from its upper surface, and movement and descent are permissible for Him. And they differed whether He fills the Throne or does not fill it, but is upon part of it? And some of them said: He is not upon the Throne but is opposite the Throne. And they differed whether He is at a finite distance or other? And among them are those who applied to Him the term 'body'; then they differed whether He is in all directions, or limited from the direction of below only, or not, i.e., not limited but unlimited in all directions. And they said: Accidents occur in His essence, and they claimed that He has power only over them, i.e., over the accidents subsisting in Him, not over those external to His essence. And it is obligatory upon God that the first of His creation be a living being from whom reasoning is valid, and besides the miracle and infallibility, and its possessor, i.e., the possessor of that attribute, is a Messenger because of his being described with it without being sent. And it is obligatory upon God to send him exclusively, i.e., it is not permissible to send other than the Messenger, and he is at that time, i.e., when he is sent, a sent one, and every sent one is a Messenger without a full converse. And his dismissal is permissible, i.e., dismissal of the sent one from being a sent one, not the Messenger, for his dismissal from being a Messenger is inconceivable.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage defines the Mushabbihah sect (anthropomorphists) as a single overarching group that likens God to created things, despite internal differences. It then lists three sub-groups. First, the extremist Shi'a Mushabbihah (as-Saba'iyya, al-Bayaniyya, al-Mughiriyya, etc.) who held doctrines of corporealism, movement, transition, and incarnation, as previously mentioned. Second, the Hashwiyya Mushabbihah (such as Mudar, Kuhmas, and al-Hayjami) who said God is a body unlike other bodies (not of flesh and blood) but with organs and limbs; they believed it permissible for God to touch, shake hands, and embrace the sincere ones who visit Him in this world, and He visits them. This extreme view is illustrated by a reported saying: 'Spare me the beard and the private parts, and ask me about what is beyond them,' implying a crude anthropomorphism. Third, the Karramiyya Mushabbihah, followers of Muhammad ibn Karram. The text notes a line about Ibn Karram: 'Jurisprudence is that of Abu Hanifa alone, and religion is that of Muhammad ibn Karram,' indicating their respect for him. Their doctrines are numerous and not taken seriously, so the author summarizes their leader's views: God is upon the Throne from above, touching its upper surface; movement and descent are permissible for Him; they differed on whether He fills the Throne or sits on part of it; some said He is opposite the Throne; they differed on whether He is at a finite distance or not; some called Him a body and then debated whether He is in all directions, or only limited from below, or completely unlimited. They also held that accidents occur in God's essence and that He has power only over those accidents, not over things external to Him. The passage then lists additional Karramiyya doctrines: God must create first a living being capable of reasoning; that being, besides having miracles and infallibility, is a Messenger by virtue of these attributes even without being sent; God is obligated to send him exclusively (no one else can be sent); and while the 'sent one' (mursal) can be dismissed from his mission, the 'Messenger' (rasul) cannot be dismissed from his status as a messenger.

Key Terms
المشبهة
التشبيه
التجسيم
السبائية
البيانية
المغيرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Mushabbihah hold the same beliefs.
Correction: The passage shows that Mushabbihah differ in method and are divided into sub-groups; the Shi'a extremists are just one branch.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a sub-group mentioned among the extremist Shi'a Mushabbihah?
A) as-Saba'iyya
B) al-Bayaniyya
C) al-Mughiriyya
D) al-Karramiyya

Key Takeaway
The Mushabbihah sect includes the extremist Shi'a who believe in corporealism and incarnation, representing one form of anthropomorphism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself picturing Allah in a way that resembles something created, even subtly? What specific thoughts or images come to mind, and how can you combat them using the lesson's warning against tashbih?
?
The Mushabbihah claimed closeness to Allah through incarnation. In your own life, do you sometimes try to feel close to Allah through physical means or emotions rather than through sincere tawhid and obedience? What is one change you will make today to seek closeness through affirming His transcendence?
?
This passage reveals that even early Muslims fell into anthropomorphism. Examine your heart: is there any belief you hold about Allah that you have not fully submitted to His revelation? Will you commit to studying His names and attributes to purify your 'aqeedah?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate

The Hashwiyya Mushabbihah
Describes the Hashwiyya sub-group's anthropomorphism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific anthropomorphic doctrines of the Hashwiyya sub-group of the Mushabbihah.

Core Idea
Hashwiyya say God is a body with organs and can be touched.

This lesson focuses on the second sub-group of the Mushabbihah: the Hashwiyya. Their beliefs are particularly crude, as they attribute physical organs and even physical interaction with believers to God. The passage illustrates their extremism with a shocking quotation.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of Hashwiyya
Read the section starting with 'ومنهم مشبهة الحشوية' and note the names Mudar, Kuhmas, and al-Hayjami. Understand their core claim: God is a body unlike other bodies, but has organs and limbs.
2
Identify the specific permissible actions
Find the list of actions they deem permissible for God: touching, shaking hands, embracing with sincere visitors. Notice how this implies physical proximity and interaction.
3
Reflect on the shocking saying
Consider the reported saying: 'Spare me the beard and the private parts, and ask me about what is beyond them.' This highlights the extreme anthropomorphism where God is imagined with human-like anatomy.
The author includes this to show the absurdity of their views.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Hashwiyya believed God has a beard and private parts, did you feel any revulsion? Now, honestly search your heart: have you ever envisioned Allah with a physical form, even unconsciously? What does that reveal about your understanding of His transcendence? How will you actively guard your tawhid against such thoughts starting today?
?
The Hashwiyya claimed God shakes hands and embraces sincere believers in this world. Have you ever treated your relationship with Allah with a casual familiarity, forgetting His majesty and incomparability? What specific change in your worship or du'a will you make to restore proper awe and reverence?
?
One Hashwiyya said 'Spare me the beard and the private parts.' Their crude conception reduced the Creator to the level of creation. Do you ever speak about Allah's attributes in a way that inadvertently limits Him or makes Him like what you know from this world? Commit to memorizing one verse about His incomparability (like Surah al-Ikhlas) and reflecting on its meaning daily for the next week.

Sects and Disagreements

The Karramiyya Mushabbihah
Describes the Karramiyya sub-group's anthropomorphic doctrines

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific doctrines of the Karramiyya sub-group, including their views on God's location, body, and accidents.

Core Idea
Karramiyya say God is on the Throne, can move, and accidents occur in His essence.

The third sub-group of the Mushabbihah is the Karramiyya, followers of Muhammad ibn Karram. Their doctrines are more elaborate, covering God's relation to the Throne, whether He is a body, and whether accidents can occur in His essence. This lesson explores their key beliefs and internal disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Read the introduction to Karramiyya
Read the section starting with 'ومنهم مشبهة الكرامية' and note the leader Muhammad ibn Karram. Pay attention to the quoted line about his jurisprudence and religion.
2
Analyze their view on God and the Throne
Identify their belief that God is upon the Throne from above, touching it from its upper surface. Notice the disagreements: Does He fill it? Is He at a finite distance? Is He a body?
3
Examine the doctrine of accidents in God
Read that they claim accidents occur in God's essence and that He has power only over those accidents, not external things. This is a unique theological position.
4
Understand their view on prophethood
Find the part about the necessity of God creating a living being who is a Messenger by virtue of attributes, and the obligation to send him exclusively. Note the distinction between 'mursal' and 'rasul'.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

They likened God to created things and compared Him to temporal things, and for that reason we made them one sect that speaks of tashbih, although they differ in their method. And they differed whether He fills the Throne or does not fill it, but is upon part of it? And some of them said: He is not upon the Throne but is opposite the Throne. And they differed whether He is at a finite distance or other? And among them are those who applied to Him the term 'body'; then they differed whether He is in all directions, or limited from the direction of below only, or not, i.e., not limited but unlimited in all directions. And they said: Accidents occur in His essence, and they claimed that He has power only over them, i.e., over the accidents subsisting in Him, not over those external to His essence. And it is obligatory upon God that the first of His creation be a living being from whom reasoning is valid, and besides the miracle and infallibility, and its possessor, i.e., the possessor of that attribute, is a Messenger because of his being described with it without being sent. And it is obligatory upon God to send him exclusively, i.e., it is not permissible to send other than the Messenger, and he is at that time, i.e., when he is sent, a sent one, and every sent one is a Messenger without a full converse. And his dismissal is permissible, i.e., dismissal of the sent one from being a sent one, not the Messenger, for his dismissal from being a Messenger is inconceivable.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage defines the Mushabbihah sect (anthropomorphists) as a single overarching group that likens God to created things, despite internal differences. It then lists three sub-groups. First, the extremist Shi'a Mushabbihah (as-Saba'iyya, al-Bayaniyya, al-Mughiriyya, etc.) who held doctrines of corporealism, movement, transition, and incarnation, as previously mentioned. Second, the Hashwiyya Mushabbihah (such as Mudar, Kuhmas, and al-Hayjami) who said God is a body unlike other bodies (not of flesh and blood) but with organs and limbs; they believed it permissible for God to touch, shake hands, and embrace the sincere ones who visit Him in this world, and He visits them. This extreme view is illustrated by a reported saying: 'Spare me the beard and the private parts, and ask me about what is beyond them,' implying a crude anthropomorphism. Third, the Karramiyya Mushabbihah, followers of Muhammad ibn Karram. The text notes a line about Ibn Karram: 'Jurisprudence is that of Abu Hanifa alone, and religion is that of Muhammad ibn Karram,' indicating their respect for him. Their doctrines are numerous and not taken seriously, so the author summarizes their leader's views: God is upon the Throne from above, touching its upper surface; movement and descent are permissible for Him; they differed on whether He fills the Throne or sits on part of it; some said He is opposite the Throne; they differed on whether He is at a finite distance or not; some called Him a body and then debated whether He is in all directions, or only limited from below, or completely unlimited. They also held that accidents occur in God's essence and that He has power only over those accidents, not over things external to Him. The passage then lists additional Karramiyya doctrines: God must create first a living being capable of reasoning; that being, besides having miracles and infallibility, is a Messenger by virtue of these attributes even without being sent; God is obligated to send him exclusively (no one else can be sent); and while the 'sent one' (mursal) can be dismissed from his mission, the 'Messenger' (rasul) cannot be dismissed from his status as a messenger.

Key Terms

الكرامية
ابن كرام
العرش
الجسم
الحوادث
الرسول
المرسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Karramiyya agreed on every point.
Correction: The passage highlights several internal disagreements among them (e.g., about filling the Throne, whether God is a body).

Checkpoint
According to the Karramiyya leader's view, God is described as being:
A) Everywhere simultaneously
B) Upon the Throne, touching it from above
C) Beyond all directions
D) Identical to the Throne

Key Takeaway
The Karramiyya held that God is spatially located on the Throne, accidents occur in His essence, and prophethood is determined by inherent attributes rather than divine appointment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the Karramiyya believed God touches the Throne and can move. Reflect: In your heart of hearts, do you ever find yourself imagining God as if He were a physical being? How can you actively purify your tawhid from such subtle anthropomorphism starting today?
?
The Karramiyya thought accidents occur in God's essence. Have you ever attributed to Allah any change of mood or emotion that implies imperfection? Will you commit to learning the correct way to affirm God's attributes without distortion?
?
This passage shows that without the Salaf's method of 'bila kayf', one falls into contradictions. Is your own aqeedah built on total submission to revelation, or do you try to rationalize every divine attribute? What is one attribute you struggle to accept without questioning?

Beliefs of the Jahmiyya on Knowledge, Attributes, and the Afterlife
Lists beliefs of the Jahmiyya on knowledge, attributes, and eschatology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key doctrines attributed to the Jahmiyya sect, including their views on God's knowledge, attributes, the annihilation of paradise and hell, and their agreement with the Mu'tazila on certain points.

Core Idea
The Jahmiyya held radical views: created knowledge, denied attributes, and believed paradise and hell will perish.

This passage from the conclusion of the fourth observation summarizes the beliefs of a deviant sect, likely the Jahmiyya. It touches on their concept of God's knowledge, the rejection of anthropomorphism, the fate of paradise and hell, and their alignment with the Mu'tazila on vision, speech, and reason. Understanding these points helps distinguish major theological positions in early Islamic thought.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow. Note the distinct claims made.
The phrase 'الله الجمادات' is uncertain; focus on the rest.
2
Identify the three main doctrinal areas
The passage covers (1) God's knowledge and attributes, (2) the annihilation of paradise and hell, (3) areas of agreement with Mu'tazila. Identify each.
3
Compare with orthodox Sunni views
Reflect on how these beliefs differ from mainstream Sunni theology, especially on the eternity of paradise/hell and the nature of God's attributes.
Orthodoxy holds that paradise and hell are eternal.
4
Summarize the sect's distinctives
Write a one-sentence summary of what makes the Jahmiyya unique according to this passage.
Include their denial of the vision of God and creation of the Qur'an.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة للمرصد الرابع الله الجمادات فيما يوجد منها والله يعلم الشيء قبل وقوعه وعلمه حادث لا في محل، ولا يتصف الله بما يوصف به غيره إذ يلزم منه التشبيه كالعلم والقدرة، لو أبدل القدرة بالحياة كما ذكره الآمدي لكان أولى لأن جهماً لا يثبت لغير الله قدرته، والجنة والنار تفنيان بعد دخول أهلهما فيهما حتى لا يبقى موجود سوى سبحانه، ووافقوا المعتزلة في نفي الرؤية وخلق الكلام وإيجاب المعرفة بالعقل قبل ورود الشرع.
Conclusion of the fourth observation. God [?] the inanimate objects among what exists of them, and God knows the thing before its occurrence, and His knowledge is created not in a locus, and He is not described with what other than Him is described, for that would necessitate anthropomorphism, like knowledge and power. If He had exchanged power for life as al-Amidi mentioned, it would be better, because Jahm does not affirm for other than God power. And paradise and hell will perish after their people enter them until no existing remains except Him. And they agreed with the Mu'tazila in denying the vision [of God], the creation of speech [of the Qur'an], and the obligation of knowledge by reason before the coming of revelation.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a description of the beliefs of a deviant sect, likely the Jahmiyya, as part of the conclusion of the fourth observation. It begins by stating that God knows things before they occur, but that His knowledge is created and not in a locus (i.e., it is not an attribute subsisting in a place). Then it says God is not described with attributes that are also attributed to others, to avoid anthropomorphism, giving the examples of knowledge and power. It mentions that if al-Amidi had substituted power with life, it would be more appropriate because Jahm ibn Safwan denies that power exists in anyone other than God (thus affirming divine power alone). Next, the passage states that paradise and hell will perish after their inhabitants enter them, so that nothing remains except God. Finally, it notes that this sect agrees with the Mu'tazila on three points: denying the beatific vision, affirming the creation of the Qur'an, and asserting that knowledge of God is obligatory through reason prior to revelation. The passage is concise and lists key doctrinal deviations.

فناء الجنة والنار

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think this sect only denied attributes, but they also held unique views on the annihilation of paradise and hell.
Correction: In addition to their denial of eternal attributes, the Jahmiyya believed that paradise and hell will eventually perish, leaving only God.

Checkpoint

A) They will never perish but their inhabitants' experience changes.
B) They will perish leaving only God.
C) They are annihilated before judgment.

Key Takeaway
The Jahmiyya sect denied eternal attributes, held that paradise and hell will perish, and agreed with the Mu'tazila on denying the vision of God and affirming the createdness of the Qur'an and rational obligation of knowing God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Jahmiyya believed that paradise and hell would eventually perish. Imagine if you were told that your eternal reward or punishment would not last forever. Would your motivation to obey God change? In what way does your hope of heaven and fear of hell actually shape your love for God?
?
The Jahmiyya insisted on knowing God through reason before revelation. Have you ever trusted your own reasoning over a clear command from Allah? What was that moment, and what did it reveal about the state of your heart?
?
They denied that God shares any attributes with creation to avoid tashbih. But consider: Do you ever find yourself imagining God in human terms, even subtly? When you pray, do you picture a being with human-like qualities? How can you train yourself to think of God as He has described Himself, without reducing Him?

The Mushabbiha: Definition and Early Subgroups
Defines Mushabbiha and lists early subgroups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the Mushabbiha sect and the anthropomorphic beliefs of its extreme Shi'a and Hashwiyya subgroups.

Core Idea
The Mushabbiha liken God to creation, but their subgroups vary in how far they take this.

The passage introduces the seventh deviant sect, al-Mushabbiha, who compare God to created things. It then breaks down their subgroups, starting with the extreme Shi'a and the Hashwiyya, each with distinct anthropomorphic claims. This lesson focuses on these first two groups and their core doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of Mushabbiha
Start by reading the opening lines where the sect is defined as those who liken God to created things. Notice that despite differing methods, they are grouped together.
2
Examine the extreme Shi'a subgroup
Identify the sects mentioned: Sabaiyya, Bayaniyya, Mughiriyya. Note their doctrines of corporealism, movement, transfer, and indwelling.
These are considered extreme even within Shi'ism.
3
Examine the Hashwiyya subgroup
Learn the bizarre claims of the Hashwiyya: God as a body with organs, and the possibility of physical contact with Him. Note the anecdote about 'spare me the beard...'
This shows how crude their anthropomorphism became.
4
Reflect on the diversity
Consider how these two groups, though both Mushabbiha, differ in their details. This sets the stage for the more elaborate Karamiyya in the next lesson.

الفرقة السابعة: منها المشبهة: شبهوا الله بالمخلوقات ومثلوه بالحادثات وهم لأجل ذلك جعلناهم فرقة واحدة قائلة بالتشبيه وإن اختلفوا في طريقه. فمنهم مشبهة غلاة الشيعة كالسبائية والبيانية والمغيرية وغيرهم كما تقدم من مذاهبهم بالتجسيم والحركة والانتقال والحلول في الأجسام إلى غير ذلك. ومنهم مشبهة الحشوية كمضر وكهمس والهيجمي قالوا هو جسم لا كالأجسام من لحم ودم ولا كاللحوم والدماء وله الأعضاء والجوارح ويجوز عليه الملامسة والمصافحة والمعانقة للمخلصين الذين يزورونه في الدنيا ويزورهم حتى نقل أنه قال بعضهم: اعفوني عن اللحية والفرج وسلوني عما وراءه. ومنهم مشبهة الكرامية أصحاب أبي عبد الله محمد بن كرام قيل: هو بكسر الكاف وتخفيف الراء وفيه قيل: متناه الفقه فقه أبي حنيفة وحده والدين دين محمد بن كرام. وأقوالهم أي التشبيه متعددة مختلفة غير أنها لا تنتهي إلى من يعبأ به ويبالي بقوله فاقتصرنا على ما قاله زعيمهم وهو أن الله على العرش من جهة العلو مماس له من الصفحة العليا ويجوز عليه الحركة والنزول واختلفوا أيملا العرش أم لا يملأه بل هو على بعضه؟ وقال بعضهم: ليس هو على العرش بل هو محاذ للعرش واختلف أببعد متناه أو غيره؟ ومنهم من أطلق عليه لفظ الجسم ثم اختلفوا هل هو في الجهات كلها أو متناه من جهة تحت فقط أو لا؟ أي ليس متناهياً بل هو غير متناه في جميع الجهات. وقالوا: تحل الحوادث في ذاته وزعموا أنه إنما يقدر عليها أي على الحوادث الحالة فيه دون الخارجة عن ذاته ويجب على الله أن يكون أول خلقه حياً يصح منه الاستدلال وسوى المعجزة والعصمة وصاحبها أي صاحب تلك الصفة رسول بسبب اتصافه بها من غير إرسال ويجب على الله إرساله لا غير أي لا يجوز إرسال غير الرسول وهو حينئذ أي حين إذا أرسل مرسل وكل مرسل رسول بلا عكس كلي ويجوز عزله أي عزل المرسل عن كونه مرسلاً دون الرسول فإنه لا يتصور عزله عن كونه رسولاً. وليس من الحكمة رسول واحد أي لا يجوز الاقتصار على إرسال رسول واحد بل لا بد من تعدده وجوزوا إمامين في عصر واحد كعلي ومعاوية إلا أن إمامة علي وفق السنة بخلاف إمامة معاوية لكن يجب طاعة رعيته له. وقالوا: الإيمان قول الذر في الأزل بلى أي الإيمان هو الإقرار الذي وجد من الذر حين قال تعالى: ألست بربكم [الأعراف: 172] وهو باق في الكل على السوية إلا المرتدين وإيمان المنافق مع كفره كإيمان الأنبياء لاستواء الجميع في ذلك الإيمان والكلمتان ليستا بإيمان إلا بعد الردة. فهذه هي الفرق الضالة الذين قال فيهم رسول الله: «كلهم في النار».
The seventh sect: among them the Mushabbiha: they likened God to created things and compared Him to originated things, and for that reason we made them one sect saying anthropomorphism, though they differed in their way. Among them are the Mushabbiha of the extreme Shi'a, like the Sabaiyya, Bayaniyya, Mughiriyya and others, as previously mentioned, with their doctrines of corporealism, movement, transfer, and indwelling in bodies, etc. And among them are the Mushabbiha of the Hashwiyya, like Mudar, Kuhmis, and al-Hayjami; they said He is a body not like bodies, of flesh and blood but not like flesh and blood, and He has organs and limbs, and touching, shaking hands, and embracing are permissible for Him with the sincere ones who visit Him in this world and He visits them, until it was transmitted that one of them said: 'Spare me the beard and the private part and ask me about what is beyond that.' And among them are the Mushabbiha of the Karamiyya, followers of Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Karram; it was said: with a kasra on the kaf and a tashdid on the ra, and concerning him it was said: 'The ultimate jurisprudence is the jurisprudence of Abu Hanifa alone, and the religion is the religion of Muhammad ibn Karram.' And their doctrines (i.e., of anthropomorphism) are numerous and diverse, but they do not reach one whose opinion is regarded or considered, so we limited ourselves to what their leader said, which is that God is on the Throne from the direction of above, touching it on its upper surface, and movement and descent are permissible for Him, and they differed whether He fills the Throne or does not fill it but is upon part of it. And some of them said: He is not on the Throne but is opposite the Throne, and they differed whether He is a finite dimension or not. And among them are those who applied the term 'body' to Him, then they differed whether He is in all directions or finite from the direction of below only or not? i.e., He is not finite but infinite in all directions. And they said: originated things inhere in His essence, and they claimed that He has power only over them, i.e., over the originated things inhering in Him, not over what is external to His essence. And it is obligatory upon God that the first of His creation be a living being from whom inference can be made, and He singled out miracle and infallibility, and its possessor, i.e., the possessor of that attribute, is a messenger due to being described with it without being sent, and it is obligatory upon God to send him and no other, i.e., it is not permissible to send other than the messenger, and at that time, i.e., when he is sent, he is a messenger, and every messenger is a sent one without full logical converse, and it is permissible to depose him, i.e., to depose the sent one from being a sent one, but not the messenger, for it is not conceivable to depose him from being a messenger. And it is not from wisdom to have one messenger, i.e., it is not permissible to limit to sending one messenger; rather, multiplicity is necessary. And they permitted two imams in one era, like Ali and Mu'awiya, except that the imamate of Ali is according to the Sunna contrary to the imamate of Mu'awiya, but obedience is obligatory for his subjects. And they said: faith is the saying of the pre-existent atoms (dharr) in pre-eternity, i.e., faith is the affirmation that occurred from the atoms when God said: 'Am I not your Lord?' [Qur'an 7:172], and it remains in all equally except apostates, and the faith of the hypocrite along with his disbelief is like the faith of the prophets because all are equal in that faith, and the two words [shahada] are not faith except after apostasy. These are the deviant sects about whom the Messenger of God said: 'All of them are in the Fire.'
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage classifies the seventh sect, al-Mushabbiha, and its subgroups. It begins by defining the sect as those who liken God to created things and compare Him to originated things, making them one sect despite differing methods. It then lists three subgroups: (1) the Mushabbiha of the extreme Shi'a (e.g., Sabaiyya, Bayaniyya, Mughiriyya) who hold corporealism, movement, indwelling, etc.; (2) the Hashwiyya Mushabbiha who assert God is a body unlike other bodies, with organs, and even claim physical contact with God in this world; (3) the Karamiyya followers of Ibn Karram, who have more elaborate doctrines. For the Karamiyya, the text details their leader's views: God is on the Throne touching it, movement and descent are possible, and various disputes about His relation to the Throne. They also assert that originated events inhere in God's essence, that God's power only extends to those events, and they have unusual prophetic theories (the first creation must be a living being who becomes a messenger without being sent, and that there must be multiple messengers and two imams). They also believe faith is the primordial covenant of the atoms, and it persists equally in all except apostates. The passage concludes by declaring these as the deviant sects mentioned in the hadith 'All of them are in the Fire.'

The Karamiyya: Doctrines of Ibn Karram's Sect
Describes the Karamiyya subgroup's detailed anthropomorphic doctrines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinct anthropomorphic doctrines of the Karamiyya, including their views on God's location, the indwelling of events, and their unique prophetic and imamate theories.

Core Idea
The Karamiyya developed a systematic anthropomorphism where even the timing of prophetic missions is determined by God's essence.

The passage now turns to the Karamiyya, the followers of Muhammad ibn Karram, who held the most elaborate anthropomorphic system among the Mushabbiha. Their doctrines cover God's relation to the Throne, the inherence of originated events in His essence, and extraordinary theories about prophethood and imamate. This lesson unpacks these complex ideas.

Guided Path
1
Read the introduction to the Karamiyya
Note the founder, Muhammad ibn Karram, and the statement about his status. Then read the first set of doctrines regarding God's location on the Throne.
2
Analyze God's relation to the Throne
The passage details various views: God touching the Throne, filling it or not, being opposite, and whether He is finite. Notice the internal disagreements.
3
Understand the inherence of events in God's essence
Learn the claim that originated events (hawadith) inhere in God, and that His power only extends to these, not external things.
4
Examine their prophetic and imamate theories
The Karamiyya held that the first creation must be a living being who becomes a messenger without being sent, that multiple messengers are obligatory, and that two imams can coexist.
5
Reflect on the nature of faith according to the Karamiyya
They define faith as the primordial covenant of the atoms (dharr), which remains equally in all except apostates, even hypocrites.

زعيمهم وهو أن الله على العرش من جهة العلو مماس له من الصفحة العليا ويجوز عليه الحركة والنزول واختلفوا أيملا العرش أم لا يملأه بل هو على بعضه؟ وقال بعضهم: ليس هو على العرش بل هو محاذ للعرش واختلف أببعد متناه أو غيره؟ ومنهم من أطلق عليه لفظ الجسم ثم اختلفوا هل هو في الجهات كلها أو متناه من جهة تحت فقط أو لا؟ أي ليس متناهياً بل هو غير متناه في جميع الجهات. وقالوا: تحل الحوادث في ذاته وزعموا أنه إنما يقدر عليها أي على الحوادث الحالة فيه دون الخارجة عن ذاته ويجب على الله أن يكون أول خلقه حياً يصح منه الاستدلال وسوى المعجزة والعصمة وصاحبها أي صاحب تلك الصفة رسول بسبب اتصافه بها من غير إرسال ويجب على الله إرساله لا غير أي لا يجوز إرسال غير الرسول وهو حينئذ أي حين إذا أرسل مرسل وكل مرسل رسول بلا عكس كلي ويجوز عزله أي عزل المرسل عن كونه مرسلاً دون الرسول فإنه لا يتصور عزله عن كونه رسولاً. وليس من الحكمة رسول واحد أي لا يجوز الاقتصار على إرسال رسول واحد بل لا بد من تعدده وجوزوا إمامين في عصر واحد كعلي ومعاوية إلا أن إمامة علي وفق السنة بخلاف إمامة معاوية لكن يجب طاعة رعيته له. وقالوا: الإيمان قول الذر في الأزل بلى أي الإيمان هو الإقرار الذي وجد من الذر حين قال تعالى: ألست بربكم [الأعراف: 172] وهو باق في الكل على السوية إلا المرتدين وإيمان المنافق مع كفره كإيمان الأنبياء لاستواء الجميع في ذلك الإيمان والكلمتان ليستا بإيمان إلا بعد الردة. فهذه هي الفرق الضالة الذين قال فيهم رسول الله: «كلهم في النار».
The seventh sect: among them the Mushabbiha: they likened God to created things and compared Him to originated things, and for that reason we made them one sect saying anthropomorphism, though they differed in their way. Among them are the Mushabbiha of the extreme Shi'a, like the Sabaiyya, Bayaniyya, Mughiriyya and others, as previously mentioned, with their doctrines of corporealism, movement, transfer, and indwelling in bodies, etc. And among them are the Mushabbiha of the Hashwiyya, like Mudar, Kuhmis, and al-Hayjami; they said He is a body not like bodies, of flesh and blood but not like flesh and blood, and He has organs and limbs, and touching, shaking hands, and embracing are permissible for Him with the sincere ones who visit Him in this world and He visits them, until it was transmitted that one of them said: 'Spare me the beard and the private part and ask me about what is beyond that.' And among them are the Mushabbiha of the Karamiyya, followers of Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Karram; it was said: with a kasra on the kaf and a tashdid on the ra, and concerning him it was said: 'The ultimate jurisprudence is the jurisprudence of Abu Hanifa alone, and the religion is the religion of Muhammad ibn Karram.' And their doctrines (i.e., of anthropomorphism) are numerous and diverse, but they do not reach one whose opinion is regarded or considered, so we limited ourselves to what their leader said, which is that God is on the Throne from the direction of above, touching it on its upper surface, and movement and descent are permissible for Him, and they differed whether He fills the Throne or does not fill it but is upon part of it. And some of them said: He is not on the Throne but is opposite the Throne, and they differed whether He is a finite dimension or not. And among them are those who applied the term 'body' to Him, then they differed whether He is in all directions or finite from the direction of below only or not? i.e., He is not finite but infinite in all directions. And they said: originated things inhere in His essence, and they claimed that He has power only over them, i.e., over the originated things inhering in Him, not over what is external to His essence. And it is obligatory upon God that the first of His creation be a living being from whom inference can be made, and He singled out miracle and infallibility, and its possessor, i.e., the possessor of that attribute, is a messenger due to being described with it without being sent, and it is obligatory upon God to send him and no other, i.e., it is not permissible to send other than the messenger, and at that time, i.e., when he is sent, he is a messenger, and every messenger is a sent one without full logical converse, and it is permissible to depose him, i.e., to depose the sent one from being a sent one, but not the messenger, for it is not conceivable to depose him from being a messenger. And it is not from wisdom to have one messenger, i.e., it is not permissible to limit to sending one messenger; rather, multiplicity is necessary. And they permitted two imams in one era, like Ali and Mu'awiya, except that the imamate of Ali is according to the Sunna contrary to the imamate of Mu'awiya, but obedience is obligatory for his subjects. And they said: faith is the saying of the pre-existent atoms (dharr) in pre-eternity, i.e., faith is the affirmation that occurred from the atoms when God said: 'Am I not your Lord?' [Qur'an 7:172], and it remains in all equally except apostates, and the faith of the hypocrite along with his disbelief is like the faith of the prophets because all are equal in that faith, and the two words [shahada] are not faith except after apostasy. These are the deviant sects about whom the Messenger of God said: 'All of them are in the Fire.'
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage classifies the seventh sect, al-Mushabbiha, and its subgroups. It begins by defining the sect as those who liken God to created things and compare Him to originated things, making them one sect despite differing methods. It then lists three subgroups: (1) the Mushabbiha of the extreme Shi'a (e.g., Sabaiyya, Bayaniyya, Mughiriyya) who hold corporealism, movement, indwelling, etc.; (2) the Hashwiyya Mushabbiha who assert God is a body unlike other bodies, with organs, and even claim physical contact with God in this world; (3) the Karamiyya followers of Ibn Karram, who have more elaborate doctrines. For the Karamiyya, the text details their leader's views: God is on the Throne touching it, movement and descent are possible, and various disputes about His relation to the Throne. They also assert that originated events inhere in God's essence, that God's power only extends to those events, and they have unusual prophetic theories (the first creation must be a living being who becomes a messenger without being sent, and that there must be multiple messengers and two imams). They also believe faith is the primordial covenant of the atoms, and it persists equally in all except apostates. The passage concludes by declaring these as the deviant sects mentioned in the hadith 'All of them are in the Fire.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All anthropomorphists deny divine power over external events.
Correction: Only the Karamiyya specifically claimed that God's power is limited to events inhering in His essence, not external things.

Checkpoint
According to the Karamiyya, what is the first creation that God must bring into existence?
A) The Throne
B) A living being from whom inference can be made
C) The Pen
D) The Angels

Key Takeaway
The Karamiyya developed a systematic anthropomorphism, including the indwelling of events in God, a unique prophetic hierarchy, and a view of faith as the primordial covenant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine God, do you ever find yourself picturing a being with spatial limits or physical features? How does the Karamiyya's explicit anthropomorphism force you to examine your own mental images of the Divine?
?
The Karamiyya insisted that the first creation must be a living being from whom inference can be made—as if God needed to prove Himself through logic. In your own life, are you ever tempted to demand that God fit into your reasoning before you submit?
?
They permitted two imams in one era, dividing allegiance. Are there areas in your life where you try to serve contradictory loyalties—society, family, self—rather than submitting wholly to one Lord? What would it look like to purify your allegiance today?
